Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these, one method is that you make three or four cauterizations in a line along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery as we have said before; and do not press your hand over the entire cautery area, and let the patient lie on his back; another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two sides, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the side where the mouse is, or where the pain of the patient comes from left to right, and let the elevations where you lift the side be according to the side, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After inserting the two heated nerves until the wound is perceived from the other side, and then draw out the cautery, and thus there will be four parts. And if you wish, you can cauterize all at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has expelled pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for someone with hydropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in the divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make four cauterizations around the navel, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the kidney; and let the cauterizations be close to the area of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open for a long time to expel impurities, do not leave the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would hasten, and both intentions would be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the abdomen should be the cleaver that we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is placed above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is hydropic, and are full of yellow water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, so as not to harm the liver, and apply the cautery in this manner:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauterizations on each leg at the point of the kneecap; and let the cauterizations be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauterizations open for a long time without healing them, so the effect lasts; then treat with the other treatments we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the diagnosis
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, such that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by usual methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach as previously described for the stomach fire cautery, a circular cautery; and four subtle cauterizations around the navel, each as fine as one small clavicle cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, perform a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each armpit, and two small cauteries near the stomach by the large area, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as we described in divisions, but it does not help, then perform cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, those that are completely outside under each hip bone diagonally, and one cautery below the navel two fingers away; and if you think their stomach is too cold, and the food does not digest, and swelling occurs in the face, then apply a large cautery near the stomach as previously mentioned, another on the liver, and yet another on the spleen for the entire clavicle length; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut into the thelul, heat the cautery until it seems like a razor, and then place it fully heated on the cut thelul; leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, from where blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large area on the flesh, it will provide greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate incision or opening, which we will recount in its place, if such a disease comes that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes to someone and is inflamed and discharges putrid matter and corrupted moisture, then you should measure it thoroughly with a probe, and be sure that you know the entire depth of the probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and apply it to the fistula according to the depth that the probe entered, and continue the cautery until all the putrid and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, depending on how much is needed; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and intestines, be careful in these areas, and do not make an incision except in flesh, and consider that it is not passable; afterward cure the area until it is healed, and if the wound is infected, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then you know that the wound is completely healed; and if the matter has not been removed, know that the condition is found, and the bone at the root is corrupted; and thus as one of those we will mention in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and there is great gas formation, and it does not respond to female treatment, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and the other with the clavicle cautery that we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauters in a line, and they will provide greater assistance.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and cold due to coldness and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then apply a cautery externally on the part above the bladder where the hair of the groin begins, one on each side, and let each cauterization be as long as the width of a thumb; and make another cautery externally on the back if you need to do so; and let these cauteries be shaped like keys according to the form described before.
de la marris	of the wheal
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the wheal is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their terminations are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and let these cauterizations be shaped like keys, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the thigh
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the joint of the thigh, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and if the source of departure is found there, then you must cauterize the patient on the joint of the thigh with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the spot around the joint as it turns, so that the joint lies within the circle; and let the cauterizations be such as those which one has used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not present for you, make three large olive oil cauterizations, and let them be as deep as all the veins; and treat until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the thigh
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the joint of the thigh, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have described in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with fetid pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you apply the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with burning medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, of which one is as follows: you cauterize on the joint of the thigh three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them with good depth and large, and there should be between each cautere a space the thickness of two fingers, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautere in the middle above the head of the thigh, for which there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier in the case of hip dislocation; but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire hip, and all the nerves be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip, and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches as far as the thigh and leg, make II cauterizations where the patient says the pain holds them, and I cauterization above the ankle IV fingers, on the left side; and let the cauterizations be circular, and burn the thickness of the nerve; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up to three or four finger widths from the sole, then cauterize where they feel the pain III points or IIII at the cauterization called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with the cutellaire or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave so much burning that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it burning so much that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it became pierced and corrupted throughout.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a belly treatment from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise said in the cautery of the thigh, concerning which here is the method, make it such iron and let it be at the head as thick as one new nail of oak, or a bit less, and let it be between the teeth and let there be from one tooth to another a space the size of one knot of wood; and let the teeth be covered on two sides, and let them also be like loops, and there should be one handle of iron well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and sparks, and then place it on the diseased side of the thigh, and turn it to the healthy side; and the cauterization once done, leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time; after treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery little due to the fear of his regard, and see few who use it; and nevertheless this is one of the good cauteries, which can bear it, and there where it applies.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make the instrument with interlocking pieces in which descends the margin of the door, and it should be made of brass or iron on one side long, and at the height have two parts, and between each should have the thickness of a finger; and they open outward and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place the hip box on the patient lying on their healthy side, and then put your hand much upon the hip box; afterwards pour between the two circles of the hot awl which has been heated in the fire a little, and leave it for one hour of time, and let the patient feel the warmth and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For there is found a burning as from fire; and when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the thigh gently, and leave it thus for three days, and put on butter until that which is black from the scalding be removed; and let him lie for three days so that pus may come out; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds warm water as you did for the thigh similarly; and this is the way of hot water, and I have written it in the chapter on the preparation of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline substances and live charcoal, an equal amount of each, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole to drain so that the point of a razor can enter; and place over that pot another lead pot, and put on alkali and heat with water above it until there is a layer of foam on top of the powder which you have taken in your hand; and leave it thus until water and bits come out of the lead pot, then take all that foam, and throw it onto alkali and heat as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be much more effective and is administered in various works of medicine and in cauterizations of other members Because it performs a different kind of work like fire, and there are other medicines with which one can well cauterize the hip such as honey anacardium and heat with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us of a cure where a man was treated for pain in the hip and sciatic nerve, and he praised it greatly, and said that no other treatment was done, and that he was cured in one session when this cure was performed, and he bathed as is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you should take green and dry litharge and grind it much with a little grease, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bandage it; and leave it on for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter the bath until his body is slightly refreshed, and then put him to bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And you should know that no one must use a cautery with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides stated that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat hair, it helps greatly; and the cauterization should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and grease it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the one called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dry goat hair and burn it to charcoal, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it turns black; and do this again, and continue doing so until you think by sense that it reaches up to the thigh, and the pain ceases; and this method of cauterization is called "goat cauterization.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from percussion or from excessive bloodletting, or from similar substances spread coldly, cauterization is not helpful in any of these cases, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient has been purged with foul pills or other similar treatments, to place on their back, where the pain lies, three lines each six inches long, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterizations be made according to the cautery which is called "poins"; and if you wish, make three cauterizations or four at the cautery clavile mean in this manner:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have difficulty lying down when they try to lie down, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in what we call the appearance which comes upon other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to treat it, cauterize it with the sponge cauterization according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cauterization affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the pricking cauterization in lines of II or III, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the area until it is healthy as we have said, and beware of applying cauterization to a swelling caused by a nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is caused by moisture spread throughout each limb, and when the pain occurs in the feet, which physicians call "gout" properly, and when it is due to cold causes and cannot be cured with medicines, then it is treated with cautery in this manner: apply the cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need to cauterize the sole of the foot, then apply the cauterization entirely with what is called a "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make a cautery on each knee III cauterizations or IV of each part, for the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand beyond when the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and the back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist II lines; and if there remains pain in both, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and proper medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it proper management and purge phlegm, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the cheekbone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a fracture occurs in the ribs, and the bowels descend to the thighs and this is recent, it must be that when you wish to treat him, he does not eat on that day; and that he uses things that loosen the belly so that his feces come out of his belly; after make him sit between your hands with his back up, and command him to hold his breath until the ribs are reset, and reset them by hand, and sew from behind near the fracture above the bone; then heat the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until they are white and until they shed scales.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and have the assistant press their hand over them so that they do not move backward; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion under him and another cloth over his thighs, and one under his buttocks which holds the hands; then apply the cautery on the spot with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bone does not protrude when you are applying the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that through this the patient does not die or suffer another harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you should know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauteries for children should be delicate according to their size, and for adults they should be proportionate to their size; after three days, treat the area of the cautery with butter until the burn is gone; afterwards, treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and have the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and ensure that they are restrained for a long time so that their eyes do not protrude when they try to move into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage and let him wear it for another forty days; and ensure he has good rest, doing little work and avoiding excessive drinking and eating, and refrain from raising his voice too much; and when he follows this advice, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment for cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other parts of the abdomen and are hard, if you wish to prevent their growth, apply the cautery according to its size, and let it burn one-third of an inch; afterwards treat it as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the location and draw a line across the width above the rupture, and another below, and evenly throughout the entire cautery area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or being injured, and that pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and the size of the cauterization should follow the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cauterization, that is well; if not, begin another cauterization on top of the previous one, for such a custom exists that the limb must change to be closer to health, so it is necessary that you perform the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of confusion
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The sick are sometimes cured by cauterization with great help, and especially the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see fit to cauterize, take care if the illness is in its beginning stages, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, do not stop or delay, and if you fear that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then apply V cauteries on the head: I at the top of the head nine times, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II on the two temples, and I behind on the occiput; and leave your hand long enough so that the cauterizations reach the bone, and until the skin comes out so that the vapors from the thick humors can escape; and apply the cautery on the armpit as it is described before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the mischief is spread everywhere; and it appears clearly, then you must cauterize with those cauters that we have mentioned at the beginning, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries above the spine of the neck, and six cauteries along the spine of the back, and one large on the buttocks and another nearby, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are above the heel, so as not to burn them; and sometimes a person cauterizes on the bone of the elbow, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauterizations you perform, the greater the help and benefit to them; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, because their body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of horseshoes.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating, apply flour of wheat with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then make cauterizations on the limb according to its size; let them penetrate slightly into the thickness of the flesh; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and foot and back, at the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; yet no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about limbs and the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of boards
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is advanced, and medicines are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery slightly deep, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with flour of barley and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and pheasant blood and lark blood, one part each; and mix them all together, and apply it with a cloth until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of a sore using cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore begins to appear and you want to stop its progress, then cauterize it with a cautery that forms a circle all around the edge of the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And still the wise say that one should make a cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and still this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before; and more prudent is it to cauterize around it, with the cautery called "circule," as we have said concerning many kinds of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it delays death either due to the excess it produces or due to the age of the patient when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to the time; and you wish to hasten its end: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; after leave it as such.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hurry to kill me.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, then heat the cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and make such a cautery that the patient feels it externally in such a way that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of disease called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a member eating disorder, for it consumes the members just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can endure cautery together with fire, then heat the cauteries to a very fine and large degree, according to what is necessary for the place where the disease is; afterward cauterize it from all sides until you reach all the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that everything that is corrupt be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized areas a mixture ground with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that no healthy flesh is growing, it is good; and if not, then restart the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this sore has sometimes been treated with a medicinal ointment instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is much more helpful, and I have already described the treatment of the medicinal ointment in the section: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of blisters that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that on the feet from outside a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a swollen thing that impedes the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterizations for this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is such that you heat it until it resembles a feather of vulture, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the nail on all sides, and there should be fine edges; after placing it very hot upon the nail, turn your hand completely around the nail until it reaches the tip of the nail; then leave it thus for III days until it begins to produce putrid discharge; then I make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the site with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted from the outside of the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you must administer hot water cautery to them; it is done as follows: take a chain of iron or steel, or a feather of vulture, place it around the nail and althea root, that is to say wrinkle warts; put the chain on so that it penetrates all around, then add a little hot water, hold firmly with your hand, press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the chain reaches the base of the nail, and let the hot water penetrate deeply down to the root; allow the patient some pain from the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will uproot itself completely along with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another, until you have treated all those who are on the body, then treat them with salves that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold, nervousness, or a quartan fever, you should perform IV cauterizations on the spine, one between each vertebra; and one on the feet, and one above the stomach at the olive cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	treatment for foul pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times, baths or foul pus-filled blisters appear on the surface of the body, which come from large corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary at first when they appear to make a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a subtle cauterization with a branch of myrtle, whose point should be seized by fire, or with a long root of aristology, or a lentil-shaped cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the excess from which they come is broken off, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut at the wound coming from outside, or from incising an abscess, or cauterizing a limb, and similar things; and it is a very serious thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to anyone, hasten to place your thumb on the wound of the vein, and press very hard until the blood is still beneath your thumb, and no more drops emerge; then put in the fire olive leaf cauterizers both small and large until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and where the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your thumb, and keep the cautery there until the blood is restrained.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you lift your thumb off the vein, and the cauterizers are extinguished, take quickly another of the cauterizers that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is restrained; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be properly stopped immediately if the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four methods we have said: either by cauterization, or by extraction when it has not healed, or by tightly binding with thread, or by applying medicines which have the power to stop blood flow; and let it be bound and compressed accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat the foul smell by tightly wrapping cloths or placing burning things upon it, or other similar things, if there is no benefit from doing so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no physician or medicine present, then he should place his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and spread it well until it is foul-smelling over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the thumb, but moisten it with very cold water frequently until the blood is congealed and thickened and becomes foul-smelling; and make a poultice from what he needs for cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to use a fire cautery or hot medicine, and the symptoms, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterizations; and I placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter in the same way so that what one seeks may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, good sirs, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterizations, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	They come from those who are so afflicted by their illness that they change easily due to the madness they find in their sickness, and because of the severity of their condition; one must be afraid of such people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these are those who regain their senses and say: "Wait, I am healed"; yet the illness is severe.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not right for you to consent to those who come to you with such behavior, but place greater care in your honor than in your desire, and do not act foolishly but wisely about those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain respect and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients where healing may be converted; and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to draw breath from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into sections, as it is before the chapter on cauterizations, which I discussed from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the child's head is held too tightly; and sometimes it happens for a reason that is not known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those whom I have seen it led to death quickly; and for that reason it seems to me that it is best to leave off working on such treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw the child whose head was full of fluid, and his head swelled each day until he could no longer hold it up; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone over the sphenoid, between the heart and the bone; and the work should be such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you split across the head a wide slit; and let it be as long as two fingers, until the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscesses are larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the seams of the head open on each side, and the fluid jumps outward when you press it inside with your hand, and this does not return to its place: then you must split across the head three slits according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After extracting the dressings of cloths and powders, and putting wine and oil on them, leave it like this until the fifth day; then remove it, treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and allow the head to drain evenly, and give the patient dried meat that has little moisture as long as the limb is becoming healthy and sound.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incising is to look at the opening of the abscess and where the fluid accumulates; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then where the abscess is open and the accumulation of fluid, and make the incision according to what you have the ability; be careful not to cut an artery; if blood flows, it may cause the patient to die from excessive bleeding and loss of moisture.
de reume	of phlegm
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone falls ill with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the nose, and the illness is long-standing, and medical treatment does no good, then the last resort is to use cauterization on both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then when you need to cut the arteries, have the patient lie down with his head back; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries become visible, and then instruct the patient to grip the cloth with all his strength; then observe where the veins are located, as they are situated behind the ears and are easily reached; mark their locations, and then cut each one with a sharp instrument from both sides, cutting down to the bone, ensuring it is done near the top of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the spatula beneath the artery and the cloth above, cutting as II should across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts upward continuously forcefully.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open upon feeling it, you must measure the quantity of space of III fingers, then cut through to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be let out is VI cotes, and perhaps a bit more or less according to what the patient can tolerate, and the engorgement of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains any point of suppuration on the bone, cut it so that no abscesses may form, then treat the wound by cleaning and bandaging, applying ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraine comes, and sharp catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and an old enraged sore and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medical care and all this does him no good, then we cut open the arteries in the temples and apply cautery, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient shaves behind the hair on his temples and listens for the artery in the temple, because it beats very clearly, except in some people who are too cold; and if it can be felt, the patient should press on its side with a piece of cloth, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and rinse the area with hot water until the artery becomes clearly visible; then take the spatula which is made as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then strip the skin gently until you reach the artery, then trace it upwards to the ligatures, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath each part; and if the artery is fine, then turn it with the tip of the hook, then cut it from that part according to the quantity of the two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then the blood does not flow completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw the blood from six places, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it must be tied in two places with a double strong silk thread so that no corruption comes before the wound heals, and there is bleeding; then cut the excess that is between the two ties at that same moment, and then, if you wish, apply the cautery of the cautery knife to the bone until the heads are cut; and this is the main work, if the patient does not have a fever and they have a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizes are helpful to finish the moistures: for this reason, they are of greater help against moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For when it is necessary to extract an artery, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when they are removed, treat them with dry medicines that promote tissue growth and apply bandages until they are healed; and if a piece of the artery is missing as you work, hasten to cut it off with a cautery, filling the area with vitriol and holding it in your hand so that the flesh hardens; and if you do not have this available, place something appropriate over the area such that the flesh freezes, and rinse the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as is necessary; and what is milder and more efficient in extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein from this cautery cutting across two parts, but ensure the cuts are well-spaced to preserve their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too cold, it holds less of its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one thick space between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places with a pin, place the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and keep them apart between the two heads because they are not joined throughout this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes come down from the veins that are above the forehead and no benefit is gained by medicinal treatment that you may apply, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel the front move as if trembling; and when the eyes are cold and moist such that the hair on the cheeks falls out, and the cheeks are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is needed.
