Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it “cure contuse,” which is that you make at the back of the patient who has this disease the hairs on his forehead, then you make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions as II do all over the forehead going down until the nose, and the other two are on each side above the temples, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are on each side above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the size of III fingers across; then have a piece of sponge and much cloth ready to wipe the blood, then place the spatula sharp at both sides as shown in this figure:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is near the temple until the second incision; and scrape off all the skin that is between the two cuts to the surface of the skull which is over the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision until the other second one, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very well suited for cutting on one side, while on the other side it is smooth, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to those near the heart, and then make another incision in the middle groove until the other side; and then draw out the blood evenly, and apply pressure to stop bleeding; then place a piece of old cotton in each groove, cover it with moistened cloths made of wine, oil, and pitch, and guard against abscesses forming; on the third day loosen the bandage and bring plenty of boiled water, then treat it with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh comes to someone frequently, and you see the eyes swollen and small, with weakened vision, and the membranes reddened; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain from a fever, and the patient sneezes; then by these symptoms you know that these matters and this catarrh come only from many veins, and if there is mucus to be treated, it is of this kind.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And when you instruct the patient to lie with his back against his forehead, then make a deep incision across the forehead, and another one on the side of the head.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision on the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two edges of the incision and put old cotton there, and cover it with linen bandages; then place damp cloths made of fabric soaked in wine and oil over it, and be careful not to get a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with substances that stimulate growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to generate flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, or stones from mines or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other substance that does not belong in the ear falls into it and does not grow within the ear, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, then drop some drops of violet oil or cumin oil, then proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze by condition, and plug their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or linen around the ear; and hold the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often force comes from this treatment; and if it does not come by force, then proceed with the extraction using fine instruments, which is described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the force of the forceps, that is good; if not, then proceed with extraction using a fine needle with a small curve; and if it does not come out even by this means, make a thread of silk and insert the tip of the thread into the ear canal firmly, and plug around the thread with soft wax so that air cannot enter through the thread; then pull forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take bird glue and place some instrument which is suitable to do this on it, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear in such a way that an abscess or spasm may come to it; and the manner of cutting is as follows: first let blood from the patient using cupping vessels according to the measure of her strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat hangs; and let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as much as possible, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and continue treating her until she is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if the grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer this thin spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And minister an incision of that abscess.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the abscess is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many incisions; then extract it with fine forceps and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute cases where water enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing to dislodge it initially, and then plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on the side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out that way, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not that way, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and easy, and warm them slightly by the fire; then place one stone in the patient's ear, and pull it out with his foot from the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come completely out; and if you wish, take a reed, and insert one end of it into the patient's ear, and set fire to the other head until the softer part of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until all the water has come out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the beast, if it is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating the distillations, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine forceps, and if none are seen, use this form of remedy:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then form it completely throughout the remedy; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out willingly, plug around the remedy with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not exit as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective against worms, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, whose form is shown as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let there be a narrow sieve of silver or brass with small holes, and above it place something to catch the drips; and for pressing within the distillation use an instrument of brass well made for this purpose, and if you wish take a razor and wrap around the tip carefully cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you want of your medicines into the funnel, and let the funnel be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press with your hand moderately until the oil is distilled at the bottom of the ear; and let the patient feel this within, and let the distillations be a little heated by fire as one distills into the ear; and beware that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffiness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with a hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to ear congestion, or when flesh grows inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes occur deep within the ear, such that one cannot see them; and at other times it happens that pus comes out of the hole, and then one can clearly see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that occurs deep inside and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many cases, and for the one you can see, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see pus present, then proceed with this spatumile as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind all flat so that it does not damage the ear; if the excrescence is of flesh from the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the excrescence is deep in the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly over fire, then apply it to the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the excrescence where the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a wick in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this on a certain day until the wound is sealed, or take a tent (medicinal application) and moisten it in rose water, and powder it with vitriol ground; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary to draw out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerate which is made of olive oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of pigeons
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althaea root that comes from pigeons' eyes when they are moist and dry, you should stretch it with tongs and pincers, and cut a piece of about one spathule of its roots; then place powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not completely removed, then cauterize with the lentil cautery and let them heal after incision; and often they repair when something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, in the paper of the eyes, things come that seem like hailstones in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is an accumulation of thick moisture above and below the paper; the treatment is as follows: watch if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is easy to know; then cut broadly, then lightly peel each part, then take it with forceps, and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the membrane, do not harm the patient; and if the incision is large, sew it up with a suture, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, make no effort, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the membrane and extract the granule with tweezers, cutting and pressing it from both sides; and if the membrane is displaced by the incision, it does no harm; and when the granule is removed, rinse the area with salt water, and treat the wound with a substance that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes above the eyes, and this happens more often with children than adults, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their beds immediately, and sleep thereon, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened by the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your two fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your lap; and then take a piece of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity it contains exinach from each part, then place it over him; and press with both hands from one side and the other so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then cut a slit in the middle of the moisture with a sharp scalpel not larger than the incision made for venesection; and cut through the skin completely until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, exinach comes out from the slit, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Draw it then in one piece of torn cloth between your two fingers to spread it out, and move your hand right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to press into the incision, so that you do not come to completely rub all of the spatumile up to the eye, so that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the incision, then enlarge the incision slightly until it appears; then draw it out as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on it, and bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is well.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to an abscessed area that is hot, treat it with soothing plasters until he is well.
des poilz des papieres	of the hair on the palms
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows on the palms that is different from what nature intended, and it becomes irritated, it harms the eyes and causes certain illnesses such as habitual tears and softening of the palms and albuginea, leading to eye damage; and the cure follows four methods: either by cautery with fire together, or by medication according to what was mentioned before in the chapter on cautery, and is done through incision and suturing or cantharides, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle along all the thread; and let this be near the margin of the paper where the hairs grow among these hairs, and draw the thread above the entire paper, and turn it to the edge; then cut in the part below the paper, below the hairs attached, across the sphenoid bone from the large tear duct to the small; then extract the thread, and place under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of a wedge, like the leaf of myrtle, and still it must be that the figure is according to the quantity you wish to lift the paper which is designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to cut off a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper has softened; then make all the spatula along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the larger tear up to smaller ones; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairline in the thickness of a root, then insert a needle into one of the two corners of the eye, and remove the skin entirely; then sew together the two edges with a needle using one fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and trim excess threads around both eyelids with some sticky substances if you wish to do so; and if not, do not worry about it, leave the sutures and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches of drying and constricting things, because the paper rises quickly from the wound's healing and its assembly, but the suture is soft (as the ancients say), and these works are done without fear; and there is another way: which is to mark the paper with a shape that resembles the leaf of myrtle, as we have described, for three inches apart according to the form that is here shown:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which protrude above the small parts equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the parts are not equal, then take a needle with thread, and insert it in the shape; and place one thread next to the large wound margin, and the second thread next to the small, and tie both threads equally; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have described, then stitch together the two edges of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hair on the paper turns: it is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one way or another requires more skill.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canthi is according to this form: you must turn the paper and cut inside as I have said, then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and tie at the two corners where you hold the threads; then carefully join one over the part that protrudes from the paper of the eye, and pull the two canthi firmly from both sides; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is stretched will die and heal and grow, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut with force, and treat until it is healed; and when the wound has closed, and if the paper has lifted, and no more hair will grow; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this measure of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and insert a thin silk thread underneath it; then join the ends of the hair and tie them together finely, and let the length of the threads be one palm in length; then arrange another thin silk thread briefly on the surface, and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient place their head in your hands; and do this near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a delicate and intricate task, then insert the needle along the follicle next to the hair, and pierce quickly through the membrane as you pull over the natural hair; then extract the hairs up to the surface of the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and does not come out with it, draw the needle entirely through to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the hair comes out from the hole above and you can see it by eye; then pull out the needle and leave a stitch behind for two days or three, until the hair grows in its place and flesh rises up; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from natural hairs, and raise it with that which you left, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pus comes in the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden opening of a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of work with it is that you should split the seam, and separate its edges, and place linen tents inside, and leave it until it heals; and in no case should you use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the illness will return worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and apply a poultice of water or ale mixed with flaxseed, and ointment made from melted wax in some oil, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you guard against it not healing according to its former form; and all the works we have mentioned are nothing but remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and it is natural causes and accidents.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, which has double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread goes through two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the entire needle, and cover with a piece about one spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks on either side of the paper; and let the edges of the two cracks be at the two corners of the incision that you have made, and make one angle so that when they are put together, the figure is as the shape of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp underneath, from what is inside the paper, then join the two separated parts with thread; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a crack or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full incision beneath the hairs of the paper, as was said above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare ingeniously with all their power how to bring back the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what requires work and instruments in various circumstances.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, you must then insert the tip of a razor underneath the skin, lifting it up; and hold it with pincers, until you cut away what adheres to the delicate membrane, without being too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient does not suffer from an overly sharp incision bleeding the eye; and make your excision, where you peel off this assembly, gently, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and heal entirely this assembly, sometimes placing salt water in the eye, and lifting it with sweet water; then place between the skin and the eye a piece of linen cloth, and put on the eye wool moistened abundantly with egg white; and after three days use poultices and soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is like frozen white moisture, such that when it is touched by iron and one thinks to remove it with forceps, it cannot be done; and both of these begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient place their head in your lap, then work with their eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then roll the nail with forceps gently, and stretch it out; then take a needle, and put some horsehair, or ox hair, or buffalo hair on it, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing all the way through, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it out, and shave off all the hair from the side of the nail which encloses the flesh and the silk to the head, then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with the fine spatula and small forceps, leaving natural flesh in the tear duct so that by the incision tears do not come regularly; and sometimes stretch the nail only at the corner, and on the thread as we have said; then shave off all the subcutaneous tissue as shown in this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatula does not touch the delicate tissue and break it, and that the probe is not pierced; and after the incision sprinkle a little ground pitch into the eye, and make a poultice of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not attached to the nerve and you cannot insert a needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail can be treated many times with medicines; it grows as I have described in the section, and if you wish to cut it, proceed carefully with the patient's eye, and take a light, sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently above, and if you see that it thins slightly and the root adheres, then drip from your mouth into the eye a poultice made of litharge and red ochre and ground pitch, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it, and first heal the hot abscess until it is healthy, then resume work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye severely, then suspend it to the nail, and cut off a part but not all, so that no blood comes out; then drip into the eye red choler made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, pressing against the eyelids and turning them outward, resembling a purple flower; the treatment is that the patient places their head in a healthy position, then works on the eyes, using appropriate hooks to coil all of this flesh, and maintaining it with force; then cut off the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting until you reach the base, being careful not to injure the eye during the procedure; make an incision as described for nail removal and small forces where bone is removed, as illustrated in this chapter afterwards; once the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply oil made from crushed seeds or similar medicines that are corrosive, then place a cotton pad soaked in egg white over the eye to prevent a hot abscess; if anything remains and there is suspicion of a hot abscess, treat it with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your work until the eye is healthy, and proceed as such for any similar growths in the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you treat each weak eye by the natural way; and in case of accident, with iron work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that cover the eye cause trouble in its function and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which the problem lies, is healthy, and there is no other disease except for this issue; then treat it as follows: instruct the patient to place their head on your hand, then suspend those veins along the entire finger according to your wisdom, and let the fingers be double fine according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two incisions be made in stages on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, when you press on those veins gently with force, and wipe the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins come out of the eye; and be careful not to damage the eye with the points of the spatula, and do this work at noon facing the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only affect those veins; and when you have done this, then pour into the eye green and red collyrium to dissolve what remains of the sore.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to do this all at once during that hour, then apply a poultice to the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is reduced and there is assurance of a hot abscess, then restart according to this method as described before until it is healed; and this is the form of applying force:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The doctor calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I said before, and it does not heal, there is pus in it that you must incise where it should drain, and extract all the moisture inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove it with all the instruments of which this form shows; and it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron bent like a knife tip, and should have points like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place over the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a bit until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the tissue is sealed and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is sealed, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that he is healthy; if this is not the case, then there is another intention to bring the fistula to the anus opening according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by means of drying medicines, and when it has been uncovered take one probe according to this form, and let the tip be in three angles, and the shaft be slender up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the temple, and keep your hand from the eye one inch away, then withdraw the probe completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if he holds his hand over his anus; and then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and hardens the tissue, let the matter go to the anus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no disturbance or reduction in vision, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply suction cups to draw out impurities without injuring; then place on the eye a poultice made of boxwood, aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and then remove the eye; and cover with bandages and cloths; and the way to prepare the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one into four layers, and then place them over each other according to how much the eye needs; then press firmly under a stiff bandage, and reapply the suction cups without injuring; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the poultice becomes loose, you must tighten it again; then remove the binding after day and night have passed, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, continue with the poultices, cloths, bindings, and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the tearing of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, it is opened up, and then paper pulp is applied as thickly as resin grains, which is terrible to see; then if you wish to repair it, work like this: insert a needle at the root of the part below until reaching above, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the side; pierce there and leave the first needle according to its position; cut around the area with double thread and tie one part of the woven cloth tightly, then remove the needle and put on wet wool soaked in plenty of egg white; leave it until the threads fall off with the woven cloth, then heal the wound with comforting things until it is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth from all sides until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in from the side of the eye, and draw out the watery humor and lower the eyelid; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but an inflammation in the eye, resembling an aqueous condition, yet it is not actually aqueous; and the manner of its appearance is such that you should seat the patient on a prepared and upright chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it gently until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then if it remains there without descending, know that it is an aqueous condition, and if the descent of the swelling does not occur as we have described.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Seat the patient between your hands, then take the spatulum and cut through the corneous skin along the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, pour into the eye hot honey mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it further as needed until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of eye fluids
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the fluids in the division, and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye tightly with one hand; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if the eye is the left one, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is the right one; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea at a distance of one hair's breadth from the white part of the eye towards the inner corner near the tear duct, and gently insert the instrument called "almagda"; turn your hand until it pierces through the white part of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches an empty space; the length of the almagda should be perfectly equal to the distance from the plumule to the end of the black part, which is the cornea; you will see the bone on the paper through the clarity of the corneal tissue, then place the instrument where the fluid is and express it out one way at a time.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, if the water rises again, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and it does not rise, gently turn your hand little by little; then add a small piece of silk gem to the water, and lift the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place behind the eye plugs made of wool soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and tie with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with egg in abundance.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almond oil cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people who have too hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but proceed delicately, then insert almond oil as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a resting place, where he can sleep on his back in a dark spot; and be cautious of all movements, and give him light foods, and let him not move his head neither to right nor left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark place, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; and it is not necessary for you to do this during the time of treatment or immediately after incision, but it is necessary to postpone this, because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses occur, that you should loosen the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who alleviates abscesses; and when it is appeased, then loosen the sight and place on it a patch for some days, and let it be in a dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and return to his normal routine; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Iraque, who told us that in their country people make an almagda puncture, through which they draw off fluid, but nevertheless I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, for those who do not recognize them; and they should be properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the front ends of these be of the same fineness, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh on the nose grows in various ways, some of which resemble many-footed scorpions; and there are such cases where the flesh is raised with a reddish hue, and there is smooth skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of this flesh that is smooth and not raised, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; work his nostrils, apply a lancet to those parts of the flesh, and draw out the filaments; then continue as much as you can with the fine sharp spatula until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be cut, treat it with the finest instrument gently, so nothing is left; and if pus overflows from an abscess, treat it as appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, act quickly and cauterize until the blood is clotted and all flesh is removed, then apply a soft and clear lotion or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostril is operated on and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not flow as appropriate, know there is flesh adhered to the bone above, which cannot be cut: then you must insert a thick linen thread, tie knots at intervals of one finger width or more, and place the patient's head in a position so that one end of the thread goes through the nostril into the mouth; many times children are taught this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the end coming from the nose with one hand, and the other end coming from the mouth with the other hand, and pull them out alternately by undoing the knots which are in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the new flesh has corrupted the old tissue, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrupts all that remains of the flesh; and then place a silver chain in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are dripped into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Whether it is made of silver or brass, it should resemble an open lamp, like a chain, and the tube should be the same; and if you wish, make a closed chain, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose and grows until it becomes large enough to be noticeable; therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove all its roots, then apply the cautery or burning medicine over it. If one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, reddish in color, and slow to respond: do not touch it with iron because it is a deeply rooted abscess, for when it is cut even once, much harm comes to the patient; but if the abscess is soft to the touch, not red in color, and you see that all of it can be cleanly cut, then empty out the patient without fear and cut it away, and treat the area with drying and constricting remedies.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the skin is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions for continuity come in one of these cartilage works, there is little benefit, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
