Then it is necessary that when this happens to anyone, you check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips in one seam, then care for it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated from both sides, you must scrape all parts of their core until they bleed, then bring together the two lips in a seam, and bind them, and put powder on powder made from dragon's blood, and ground incense; and place the powders under a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it comes off by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is that you bring together the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suturing of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In some people, there is a hard abscess on the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut into each node, grasp it with forceps, and cut it in each part; then fill the area after incising with powdered vitriol until the blood stops flowing; then clean the area with rose water, and treat the wound with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a piece of flesh grows on the gums that the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the blood or pus to flow; then apply vitriol powder ground up, or other powders that constrict and dry; if this flesh returns after cutting, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize: it will not return after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of filthiness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the roots of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, crusts that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black or yellow or worm-eaten until corruption reaches the gum and the tooth becomes foul-smelling; you must seat the patient between your hands, and hold their head in your lap, and remove the teeth or crusts thoroughly, so nothing remains; and thus clean the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are clean; if you extract what needs to be removed at first sight, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and third, until everything has been cleaned out; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for removal, depending on the work that needs to be done, because the tools used to remove teeth between the teeth are different from those used to remove them by extraction; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing it out as much as you can, for one must not do this; for it is a very high substance until there is no excuse for pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to have it drawn out, you must be certain about which tooth is causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain constrains the patient, and they believe it to be in a healthy tooth, so they have a good tooth extracted; but the pain does not leave them by this means until the bad extraction is corrected. And when you are certain about which tooth is causing the pain, you should char around the tooth for about one span very strongly to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or small pliers little by little until it is well loosened, then secure the pliers firmly; and hold the patient's head in your lap between your knees, and hold them still so they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and push on each side gently, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, you must fill it with cloths where the hole is; and gently extract it with pliers so that it does not break when extracted; and carefully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave part of it behind, which would return to the patient causing greater pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not act as the ignorant practitioners do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the tissue, and do not follow what we have described; instead they cause at times severe illness due to the roots remaining or because of the tissue they break, as we often see; and when the tooth is extracted, clean the area with wine or hellebore and salt; and if bleeding persists, which often happens, fill the area with ground vitriol; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to extract teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not double back when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-forged iron, and should have teeth to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary to place cotton soaked in butter on the site for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the gum softens, then you can insert the forceps called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument that is called "althali," which is known as a scalpel, of which this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, of which the forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are mentioned before in the context of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of bone are; and also other instruments which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their work and the illness shows them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of some, or if one breaks of the carriage or of other bones, it may rot, so seek among the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-constructed to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to its natural position in the body, and its form is ugly, especially in maiden women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after another tooth and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or polished: then split it; and if it grows out of line with the tooth, take this instrument here which looks like a small beak, and let it be sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it a little at a time over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, then file it with a file like this one.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth a little at a time over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks off; then smooth out any rough edges with a plane for all files, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth grind
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth grind, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press upon what they chew without defecating, and you have treated them with constrictive medicines but to no avail; then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold thread, for silver wire becomes green and rots, but gold never moves; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and loop it double between two healthy teeth, then place the knot between the damaged teeth, if there is one or more, carefully until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering until you return to where you started, and gently but skillfully tighten your hand so that nothing moves; and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the wire with pincers, and join them together, and place them between healthy teeth so as not to touch the tongue; and then leave it tightly bound for as long as possible, and if they come loose or the thread breaks, tighten it again with another piece of thread; thus it will remain and serve in this manner throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and of the two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, place another fresh tooth in its place as we have said; and do not involve anyone who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from the bone of a cow's knee, places it where the deficiency is, tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is a time when this ligament that comes from under the tongue exists since birth; or due to an accidental wound that has healed; and the procedure is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your hand, then lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament broadly, until the tongue is detached from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, which is due to the sudden healing of a wound, insert a hook and cut it broadly in that manner; be careful not to make too deep an incision, for the artery lies below; and when you have finished, lift out any pus with rose water and myrtle juice, or cold water, then place under the tongue a pad of linen; and change this dressing every night so that the wound does not close up.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place over the area vitriol ground up; and if the blood weakens him, then cauterize with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it as a black or hard color and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it inclines towards blenorragh and there is moisture, then apply lancing to it, and cut it with a fine spatula, and free it from both sides; and if his strength fails you in your work, place on vitriol ground up until it cools down, then return to your work until you treat all the force; then lift the area gently and carefully, and treat it with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	At times, lumps come into the throat which are called "godath," and these are properly referred to as the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess with a small sensation and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the base is swollen, do not touch it with iron, nor for bloodletting; but leave it until it turns black, and then you will remove it, as it would break by itself; and if it has a white color and the base is delicate, prepare the instrument to cut, but first see if the abscess is resting and has subsided.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his head be in your sight, and work with his mouth and grasp him by the jaws between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, which is of this form; and it should be of silver or fine brass as sharp as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see an abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the almond area, and pull out more than you can; and draw some things from the tissue with it, then cut along the instrument, which is of this form, resembling forceps; and yet the ends are curved, one end opposite the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pliers, here is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cutting on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, cut the other in the same manner, then after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and soothing water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water containing pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then treat it until he is healthy; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two glands, so cut them as you would the two glands equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was born inside her throat, which is to say the tonsillar abscess; and I found it almost completely closing off the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had risen two fingers' width through the two passages of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurried then and inserted a lancet into one nostril, then pulled it out forcefully, removing a large amount of pus; then I did the same on the other nasal passage, stitched up her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the lancet into the abscesses, removed some part of them, but only a little blood came out; thus, the throat conduit was unclogged for the woman, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting into this abscess over a long period; the abscess grew back quickly and filled up the space that I had emptied until it became very large again; then I reinserted the lancet and cauterized inside her throat: thus it remained without growing anymore; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did for her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye睑户 kvinde<|im_start|><|im_start|><|im_start|><|im_start|>
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is detached, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the diffuse abscesses are subsiding, and they are subtle, then you must cut them; and those that are round and assembled and are not elongated; and if they are bloody or of a dusky color or black, then you should avoid cutting them.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, regarding its blueness and length, make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously; then pierce the onion in the eye, and draw it out from below, and cut it at I of the II instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the II almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut beyond the excess that is over the natural limit; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the II almonds, and treat it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use skill in the cautery to calm their fearful sense.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cautery is acute ague.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient place his head in your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cover it with vinegar-soaked cloth, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and around this implement, here is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the head a cloth where the medicine is applied, as much as would fit on a spoon, and put the instrument over all the medicine onto the eye; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine without it going down his throat; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it absorbed and the irritation of the medicine subsides. And if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and apply the instrument with the cotton to the eyelid, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; do this often as needed for the cautery to be complete, then leave it to dry, and after four or five days remove it. If you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, start again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse it with cold water, and gargle until he is well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation according to this method, take calamus and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather them all in one pot or some of them, and add water, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be an instrument made as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper, and place one end in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the affected area through the vein, until the affected area is necrotized; then repeat often, until the affected area dries up, and beware that you do not perform this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things may happen; and do not do it except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a chain and place inside the head an eggshell so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and this is both good treatment and safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or some other thing gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must extract what you can see, and press the tongue with sunlight all over the instrument so that you can see the object moving; and for what is not clear and remains in the throat, you should make the patient vomit as if the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the stuck thing through vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a lettuce root, or a dry bread crumb; tie a thread to the sponge and then have it swallowed; when it reaches the spot, it will stick to the object, and then pull out forcefully; if these methods do not work as we mentioned, take an instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it may more easily enter the throat, and hold the tip upwards; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, nor push the bone in; and move slowly that the patient may place the instrument, for if he is moved when the thing is sharp; if you push down, do so evenly along the entire length of the instrument.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I said in the division, by curing it with medicines; and when this does not help, then examine the patient's throat in sunlight, pressing the tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out completely with a small hook or with fine forceps.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hooked cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then place a hot iron on the hook of the cane, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is to be treated with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full bottle of cold water and pour it into the mouth, allowing it to be swallowed, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of grapes; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take one pot which has live coals, and cover it with a perforated lid, in which there is an aperture for the instrument's tube; then pour your fumigation into it, and have the patient place their head at the end of the tube, and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes only to the blood; and now the blood will fall out, and if it does not fall, restart the fumigation many times; and allow the patient thirst, and eat salted and sour things, and do not drink water; and then by this governance it will be necessary for it to come forth.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, when it can be seen, resembles curved tongs for entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and there is roughness like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and here you see the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory brings forth later in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and this is in two ways, one of which is in its form itself, and from those it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is according to the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses in soft tissues are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are others that should be pierced when they are hardened, and do not die off according to their completion, such as those near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is thoroughly rotten, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay puncturing it until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the fundament, puncture it as soon as it dies; but do not pierce an unripe abscess before complete digestion, except for one near the fundament, so that it does not rot completely, become elongated inside, and cause a fistula; and cannot heal in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for puncturing an abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, the fever has abated, there is a decrease in pain and redness, softening at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary to perform the puncture where the abscess depends most, and where it appears mellow; and the puncture should be long on the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no thinness.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases of bleeding, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better to wait until it is confirmed to be fully digested before performing puncture, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that time, the body of its venom will be elongated, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance its lips and depth may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that should be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses that require cutting deeply, and excising; when they become as hard as leather and are softened, it is necessary to do as with boils: and there are some that are cut into three angles, and there are others that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, as in the case of arm abscesses; and there are those where a round incision is made, and other types of cuts and similar excisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have a superficial and small abscess should be thoroughly punctured by you; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not extract all the pus at once, but extract some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then extract something again; do this gradually over many times, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is weak in constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men who are feeble.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes spurts out suddenly with the release of the pus, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not hold yourself responsible for it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; if it is a simple incision, then apply linseed or old cotton dressings; and if there are large abscesses with many openings, then place a dressing in each opening so that they come together; and if you have cut into the skin around the abscess, and you have sewn it up, then fill it with dry lint or linen shreds without moisture, and tie it for three days; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, then administer cold and soothing water, and wet the cloth, and apply it to the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is winter and the area where the abscess is located is very nervous, then you must place tents and cloths moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is summer and the area is fleshy, then you should apply cloths wetted with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said. Then open the abscess and wipe and treat it properly until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of sweat
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small abscesses on the head come in various forms that are like the webbing of a goose's foot, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and have moisture like pus; and there are others that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt unless the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the waist is such that you must test all the instruments called "entromissoire," of which the form follows hereafter, as to what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then he cuts it from above along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied out, then scrape without leaving any part of the skin that contained the moisture, for it returns quickly if anything is left behind; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, use water and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will heal what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart with the cotton as before on the second day, and continue on the third day, until you are sure that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is in fatty tissue, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and pour on your ointments, and peel it all around, and apply all your care to draw out from under the skin where it lies; and if an artery obstructs you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for an abscess if it contains stones, cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting into a stony abscess and moistening it, it is easier because they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses are in the head where there is no moisture, and among these were the abscesses that I cut from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had struck any part of it, they would have as easily made a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, whether those that come to the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be made as low down as possible, so that the pus may exit; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	This type of abscess often occurs in the neck, and sometimes under the armpits, and also in other places on the body, and they are very painful, and grow one next to another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, as the knot and the head abscess are, as we have said; and there are many varieties of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not wish to obey healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one that you see has good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the skin, and soft on all sides and is not hard against the neck arteries or veins, nor deep; then it is necessary for you to cut above it, and peel the skin from each part, stretch the two lips of the wound with forceps if you need them, as we have said regarding abscesses on the head; and make small cuts and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not let the scalpel be sharp or cutting too deeply, so that your hand does not slip, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, put in the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softened, and then begin to treat it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is clotted, then return to your work, until you complete it; then seek with your proper instrument if there remain any small scrofulas, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then it is not right that you should cut this scrofula at its root, but tie it off with strong double thread, and let it fall away without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the whole scrofula, then you must bring together the two edges of the wound and suture them now, since there is no excess tissue due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary for you to focus on cutting the root of it, extracting the pus, and suturing as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For scrofulas that contain excess tissue, pierce where it appears to be most decayed; and treat the puncture as previously described, allowing for drainage, then administer treatments with ointments and similar remedies so that what remains of the corruption decomposes; and when the wound is thoroughly cleansed, cure it with healing ointment until it is healthy.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the treatment of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who performs it, and this is their writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit in the throat which is called "epiglottis" be removed; and one should not help them with this, because all the veins and the flesh of the patient are affected by hot abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision across III circles or IV, between the II circles or according to the size of the incision on the surface, not in the cartilage; and those parts are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from end to end.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the neck for its entire length, then cut through until he reaches the trachea; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm in the trachea which flows out from the place that is ruptured, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which strangulation is feared, bring together the two edges of the wound of the heart, and suture entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim states that one should not do this until the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and death approaches.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus saved from death; and for this reason the elders commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness passes, which takes three or four days, and then they command to sew up the wound and clean it until it is cleaned; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the veins there; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out, and I saw clearly that she had not cut any vein or main artery of her throat, and the flesh was issuing forth from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and stitched the wound, and treated her until she was healed; and nothing happened to the lady but that she lost her voice for a time, and returned later to her senses; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis there need be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the shape of a bean, and it occurs frequently in women; and it exists in two manners: natural and accidental; the natural one does not have a head.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one exists in two manners, of which one is similar to our fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from a vessel; and there is fear, and it should not be treated by cutting except in the case where it is small, and you prove and search throughout the interior: if you find it as our fatty tumor, and it cannot be drained through any vein, then cut it out, just like one cuts out tumors, and remove all its covering if there is any; and examine thoroughly, and treat it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways, of which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to speak about all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that after the fever and heat persist until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own sac and matches the color of the skin, and begins like a pimple, and grows large; and they are similar in appearance, either hard or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of the nose that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to how their form will appear in the chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of investigating abscesses of the nose is that you take where it is most moist in the abscess, and press with your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful not to use excessive force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture flows out when it runs, whatever color it has, proceed as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly peel it on each side and be careful of the coat where it lies so you can draw it out whole with the nose; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then remove it piece by piece until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the inflammation returns repeatedly; and if a little remains and the blood does not grieve, apply the wound with some corrosive powders and cleanse the wound, and place hot compresses to ease the abscess, and treat it with other methods until it is healed; and if the inflammation is severe, sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it as one who generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein resists or another issue arises, hurry and apply a place treated with broiled vitriol, and leave it for two days or three until the wound becomes rotten, and let the blood boil; then return to cleaning what remains of the inflammation.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments used for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb," which also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses from fistulas; and they are like the needles used to sew sorceries, and are made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and for encircling the curves of fistulas, black lead is more effective; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of hooks are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks that have two curves in three ways likewise; and there are hooks that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are hooks that have two curves, and hooks with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these for cutting is sharp, and there are some that cut only from one side, so as to peel the skin, so that when opening an abscess, neither the vein nor the nerve is cut; and these intramural ones have alembics suspended by handles, so that the patient does not feel them during the incision of abscesses; and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see; and one uses them only in soft tissues such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling the rind of a citron, according to this form, which stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed at the site suitable for cutting veins, and arteries, and sometimes follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the testicles of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them must proceed according to this form from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicine that promotes flesh growth to the wound, then bring together the two edges of the wound into a seam, and treat it until it is healed; and if the testicle hangs down due to its size being like women’s, make two incisions above it with similar cuts; so that one end connects to the other at both ends, as shown in this form from line b to line g; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and proceed as we have described for suturing and powders, and what is necessary for treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision has not been fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to excessive bleeding, you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in a caustic ointment; leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that appear under the buttocks are hard forms of scrofula with sides, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be incised according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment appropriate for healing until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, then incise it as we have said for scrofula incisions, and if the wound produces pus, then treat it with cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sealed, abscesses often occur; similarly, this happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. And when you recognize it as being due to the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you can sense its firmness; and when it is caused by the vein, it appears soft and diffused; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, at angles, on the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
