and then move with your right hand inside the abdomen of the scrotum, extend the hard white fat tissue high to your left hand, lift the testicle up along the waist; and instruct the assistant to lift the testicle up and release what is tied at the back; and ask if any part of the intestines are wrapped around the hard white fat tissue, and if you find anything, put it under the abdomen below; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it into the rear part of the fatty tissue, which is behind the skin of the scrotum, after the waist, cut the threads that appear from the strands until there are four strands left; then arrange them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and tie up the fatty tissue about which we have spoken, which is under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong thread on two sides; then wrap around the threads of the strands tightly on both sides so that no worms that cause abscesses can enter the wound; and put back the bandage according to the first long bandage by two fingers of its length, and after these two bandages leave the fatty tissue under the abdomen one finger wide; and afterwards cover all the rest according to the roundness that the scrotum bears; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the scrotum until you reach the vein and the bowel, as we have said before; then apply moistened linen dipped in oil on the wound, and place back the bandage as instructed.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white skin we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and let the ligament heal by itself until it falls off; and if it delays in falling off, then soak it with hot water, and apply what we have said until it falls off; then treat the wound with another method until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the condition involving the intestines, in such a way that you bind the vessels, above the waist lightly on top; then cut into them, and treat the abscess as we have described, until the vessels release; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin area, as we have said, and it is apparent; and no part of the intestines descends to the genitals, and if they do descend, it is an emergency that requires immediate attention at all times; and still, if it remains too long in this state, the wound or rupture will worsen until the intestines descend. This happens due to the extension of the groin area where the rupture occurs, as we have mentioned, because it becomes stretched, then softens and swells up visibly; and treatment for this is through cautery, as we have previously discussed; and sometimes it is treated with an iron in this manner: and that when the patient lies supine on their back between your hands, you cut around the swollen area of the rupture about three fingers wide; then extract the tissue beneath the skin carefully, then take the needle and place it over the visibly affected area of the groin; press firmly onto the abdomen, then sew up both visible sides of the groin wound over the head of the needle, sewing one side first and then the other; then remove the head of the needle without cutting more of the tissue or stretching the skin any further, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal prolapse; then treat it like a regular wound.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then disinfect and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is constrained, and there is no appearance of it in the rupture, and the cauterization is cold in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the genitals often softens in some men because the tissues inside become softened and appear milky; and when one wishes to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, then cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you wish, sew off the excess softened skin along three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is condemned in our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; yet it is necessary for two reasons: one is that the physician must know how to respond when asked about it and how to treat it; and the other is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we perform castration by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become soft and hang down; then grasp them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: it is necessary that you geld the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each one at a single stroke when they have been well flayed; and leave some of the fat under the skin and the subtle fat which is on the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that which is done by traction, because in traction there may be left behind some part of the testicles, due to which the animal desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermpheidry is according to two manners in men: one is such that between the two testicles it has an opening as the figure of a woman's body, where there may be hair, and sometimes encircles the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and place upon the belly as with a rod and two eggs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for a man and a woman is that you cut away the adjacent tissues and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays over the skin of the genitals, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tension or strain
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue attached to the genital area, so much so that it is too deformed to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should stain the excess of the tentigene with your hand or fingernails and cut it lightly; do not go too deep that blood comes out, then treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed; and for another tissue that grows at the entrance of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may bleed, and it resembles a quill, hence they called it "quill disease" by the ancients.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said about tendinitis, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman's body is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has come upon her; or it is caused by flesh adhering, or from fine or thick phlegm, and formed in the belly, or ribs, or within, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and knowledge of this is gained through examination.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstruction is close to appearing, then I desire it to be removed by your hands or straightaway.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle syphilitic sore and it is near the two buttocks, hurry, and do as follows: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch out the two buttocks fully, so that the subtle sore is exposed, and be over the suppositories; then take linen, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the area, and lay the woman face down each day, so she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sore is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a scalpel similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the suppository is flesh-based, suspend it on a needle and cut it; and have medicines that constrict bleeding, such as vinegar, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with plenty of egg white; then dress the wound with a strip of cloth wide enough so the wound cannot close; and thus treat it for an extended period, and dress the wound with a piece of dry linen; then continue treatment with other methods until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh is wounded in the marsh, it should be treated according to this method, except for embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the case of an embedded abscess in the marsh, one should not attempt to lance it.
des emorroides	for hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that often occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids become old, they harden; and I have already mentioned in the division their appearances, and the signs, and here I will say those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when hemorrhoids and hard lumps are perfectly formed in the marsh area, and they do not respond to sensation, then treatment with a cautery iron is not appropriate.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have the mouth of the boil, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by draining.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the altar with tongs, and cut it at its roots; then apply medicine to constrict blood flow, such as oak bark, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then keep her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, gall, and similar substances; then take oatmeal, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if the bleeding stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have the patient lie down and apply cupping to the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, and mix it with juice of plantain or agrimony with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has rested, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and what is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard head, so it must be lanced as I have said about the thulul; then continue to treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as cankers and stone-filled abscesses and herpes and carbuncles and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not of the kind that bowe collects; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let the abscess die down until the pain is eased; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and give him two small chairs where he can recline, and support his back and bring together his legs behind the thigh; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them securely with a good bandage; then give him some medicine towards the right side, and administer the instrument used for treating the mouth of the marrow, which is described below; and it must be that when you wish to use this instrument, you insert its tip first to determine the depth of the marrow so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than necessary, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it should cover the depth of the marrow with cloths so that the instrument does not cause pain; and it must be placed at the top of the instrument, and you should hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut with a gentle hand, one must then slice off the top, the spatumile layer; and when the pus is emptied out, you should place in the wound moistened cloths soaked in rose oil or green oil; place the cloth towards the wound at the depth of the flesh, and above the flesh and on the finger use clean wool moistened with water or mallows boiled; then treat after two days of ointment application as needed, until it is healed; sometimes lift the flesh and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then with water in which roots of lilies and plantain are boiled for a long time; then return to the ointment treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed in the flesh, you must avoid treating it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the natural figure of childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downward, and desiring to smell the air: then the child hastens to come forth; at that time you know that this childbirth follows the natural course, and the passage is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, it is fitting to press lightly on her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for as soon as it descends by its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities through proper care; and one who arrives otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and comes forth with the body or the buttocks, and the hands, or it may come out on her belly, or from below, and is turned about by chance onto its neck, and in other evil positions; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally on its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, where women usually hold; and prepare for her an ointment from oil or fenugreek cooked, and then apply between her two cheeks the small spatula which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the second membrane, and slice to the nail until the moisture inside comes out; and press the woman's belly so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek musilage mixed with sesame oil; then have her inhale and sneeze from condii, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands issue forth, it is necessary that you reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up high; then lift the chair off the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when lifting; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here before, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of delivering the child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to press it upwards; then turn it little by little until it is straight; then take one of its feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, then command it to be caught, and make it sneeze with cold water; if it does not jump out, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it comes out easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take muscillaginous of altai, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind everything in the mortar; then place the woman's nature within this ointment and outside apply this salve, then make her sit in hot water up to below her ribs; when she is moistened below, give her a collyrium of myrrh, and put it underneath, and leave for an hour; then make her sit on the chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently massage her abdomen, for now the child will jump out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child upon his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place the woman's hands little by little on the ground; then she should lean back on her neck, and let her feet hang down, and lie flat on the bed; and bend her hands little by little, and then hold her hands on her belly, and remove the cushions beneath her, until she is prepared to go lower; and if the child does not come out, take her feet and move them apart, then lift her belly upward, then put your hands in; and bring out the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold onto you as much as possible until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the engineer to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her on the bed, and straighten her legs completely; then apply the massage that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and according to the natural figure of the child, make her sneeze, and command her to grasp tightly so that the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on her neck, and have her hands spread out, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the baby to hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and move it gently; and when it is even, apply the natural massage of altitude and oil as we have said, then command her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command her to grasp tightly; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying heat in this manner to the entire second part, cut the second part at your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the fetus can move on its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not obstructed and move the fetus; then place the child inside as it should be, and instruct the woman to grip a few times: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	on the outcome of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins often give birth multiple times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, it happens occasionally.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if one can name them; I know that they multiply, and are separated by the surface which divides them, which is attached to the bud; and sometimes they issue as naturally as other fruits, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue painfully, then treat them as we have said, and let the nurse be subtle, and do quickly and gently what she does; and act as it is necessary for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are completely formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise glory, and it is necessary that the nurse knows all this, because similar things may happen; so act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained by manual work; then it is necessary to know if the woman is in good health and has no accident that causes fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, with her knees bent downwards, and her legs raised; and the assistant holds her hands from two sides, so she does not slide down while the child descends; then rub her mouth with oil mixed with musk of aloes and fenugreek seeds and flax seed, then anoint her arms with these oils and these mixtures; then place your hand gently in the oil and mixture, then find a suitable spot where you can apply the hooks, and check if the child is prepared to come down headfirst; then insert the hooks into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the nape or near the ribs, and if the descent is from the feet, place them at the wrist and middle ribs; it is necessary that she holds the hook with her right hand, places the curve between the two fingers of her left hand, and gently pushes it all with her hand, placing the hook in any of those spots we mentioned until it reaches an empty space; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other needle, or a third if you need one, so that the extraction is equal; and then extend it equally by moving from side to side, for the hairs to come out, and let the needles be toothed to hold the hairs, as shown in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, anoint the edge of one of its sides with oil, and press it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if any part still remains, place this needle higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and it cannot be returned for gripping, you must wrap around the finger until it comes out completely; then cut at the joint of the knuckle or at the base, and similarly, you must do this with the other hand, and with both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow in the passage, when there is a fever gathered in the head, then you must insert the spatumile between your two fingers, cut open the head, and draw out the fluid; or you can shave it with the instrument called “almidach,” about which the forms come with the instruments in the chapter after this one; and thus do if the child has a large head naturally; then pull apart the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps forth and is held by the muscle, cut through as far as the moisture that is in the passage; and if it cannot flow out, cut it off piece by piece until you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the belly or chest, then you must stretch it with a sling wrapped around your hand; and cut into the belly or chest until the moisture inside escapes; and if another member has been removed, and the head remains, then put your thumb firmly in the socket, and pull it to the mouth of the socket; then insert one finger or two, and pull straight out; and if the mouth of the socket is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, then do not work on it, but instead administer moist and fatty things; and apply remedies such as plasters, and soak in warm and softening liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it even, then treat it as we have said about the living child; and if one has no power, then cut it into pieces, and leave nothing of the membrane.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said about large abscesses that come with fever; and if bleeding occurs, place it in constricting water, and treat it with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus in her womb had died, then another was conceived afterward, and that one too was stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her cheek, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to severely purulate.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought about it for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an adhesive plaster, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was at a good point of recovery; and I treated the woman for a long time in this way, and she would occasionally discharge some fluid from the site; and I have not recalled this chapter other than because when masters encounter an unusual thing, they should seek to understand it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which is used in the books; and for two turns at the two shoulders of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the binder, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the wood one finger thick, and in length a palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two fittings of the same shaft, which are firmly set on both sides, about half a palm long or a little more; and these two fittings are inserted into the mouth of the joint to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling the forceps; and it should have two heads with attachments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the mouth with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then place the two attachments together in the mouth, holding the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the forceps equally, according to the size you wish to open the mouth of the woman, until she gives a face as she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all designed at the top, and their appearances vary widely; and when the doctors have them prepared, the work is done more quickly, and they are more effective for people in terms of their quality.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze by administering something appropriate, and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, so be it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its cover, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as camomile, rue, anise, chamomile, savory, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled or brewed in water over fire; then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mare's mouth, and hold it so that the vapors come inside the mare; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move as commanded, instruct the patient to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or muscilaginous of hellebore, and then place it on the area, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straightly so that the stiffness does not hinder extraction; but it must be moved gently to right and left, and then drawn; it will come out and release itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the joint of the stiffness is tightly closed, we have mentioned the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move despite everything that we have said, do not force pulling; but what is at the mouth of the stiffness must be tied to the woman's thigh, then administer a clister of tetrafarmacos ointment; this will soften and reset it, and it will come out; however, when she passes gas if there comes an unpleasant odor in the stomach and head, it harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are necessary for these cases: some of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers and secondine is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a tube, and the tip is fine in its nature, while the ends are wide over the fire; and place the fumigation above the coals, and let the smoke be produced until it is exhausted, then begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but instead it is blocked by a small sphincter: therefore, the midwife must pierce that sphincter at its proper place, and should not use a sharp spatula, being careful not to injure them; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, followed by ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you fear that it will not hold, place a chain of lead in the hole, and leave it there for days, and remove it when the patient wishes to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from the sudden closure of a wound or abscess; it is necessary to cut that closure: it should be treated as we have said about the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the anus are nodations, and those that come near the anus to exit or in between the two parts may have one fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it works, and still retains moisture as white or subtle mucus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; they are known by what comes out during defecation or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and perhaps a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and reach to the knee joint, and to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one can know whether the fistula extends to the anus or not: and it is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and inserting a fine needle of silk or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, insert a thread of fine linen or horsehair until you feel the thread at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no evacuation occurs from either flatulence or stool as we have said: then you know that it does not penetrate; hence hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the channel of urine, then urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then the pain comes up to that place; if there is no twisting and the source of the pain is around it, then it will immediately become a boil, and medicine or salve applied does no good; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure except for labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not penetrating and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is so that the patient lies on their back; lift their legs up to their thighs, and incline their thighs towards their belly; then insert a probe of linen or lead if there is twisting, until you know where the probe goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should place your thumb there, and if you sense that the tent has been pierced; and where you feel between your thumb the surface or flesh, then know it is perforated; do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says always that some can be well healed, but this happens rarely; and the help one gives is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and insert it entirely hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that the unhealthy tissues are burned, which appear like a feather quill; and then treat with tents moistened in butter, until these unhealthy tissues disappear, then treat with an ointment that heals flesh and binds.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that cannot be otherwise for him to be healthy; and if the fistula enters, but does not reach the deepest part which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fatty tissue between the anus and the fistula; when you see the fistula under this covering of the heart area, cut it from the beginning of the fistula, then push forward through the fistula, and apply the cautery afterward until it reaches the head of the fistula; then the fistula will be released and fall out. Afterwards, clean away the damaged flesh that looks like a feather quill, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood fails you, and congeals between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with a hot medicinal agent.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery unites two good things: that is to say, it burns away harmful substances, and stops blood and dries up moisture; then treat with bandages soaked in butter or crushed herbs until the wound oozes pus, and thus the burned flesh comes out in the pus; then heal the wound with hardening ointments applied as plasters.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up from the deepest part of the fundament, and is distant from the body, then pierce it there at the fundament, and inquire into its extent.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the bandage, and there are two layers of tissue or skin between it and the deeper tissues, where it is close to piercing through, do not act hastily without faith and hope, by following one of the three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut it down to its base, or if you can place a bandage and treat it as initially described; but do not go too deep, that you might cut into the tissue holding the fundament, and allow natural healing to occur as intended; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering after cutting around the fundament, either by bandage or with another instrument designed for this purpose; then clean the diseased flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study how to restore the wound and divert the fistula away from the fundament: this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the bottom of the foundation near the skin above, then take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread in a spiral from one to two, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perpendicular at the edge of the foundation inside, then remove the thread from that opening, so you place your finger on the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold them to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and tighten it occasionally, until the thread matches the flesh between them and they heal; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make an incision too deep for the discharge, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous process where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other side, because one should not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: some are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they contain blood, either one or several; others are outside the anus at its edge; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes contain a bit of yellow water or a bit of blood, and their color is like flesh. The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit in baths until the hemorrhoids swell out and become visible; then grasp them with forceps at your nail, and cut them off at their roots; if the forceps cannot hold them due to moisture, take a probe or cotton or some piece of lint, and extract them with both hands, then cut them, and apply warm powder suitable for cauterization; proceed as described in the chapter on cautery, and treat further until they are healed. If the hemorrhoids cannot be expelled from the anus, administer an enema of a harsh and rough solution to clean what is inside the anus so that it can come out easily. When the patient sits down, if the filaments have come out of the anus, treatment is easier; grasp them with your nail or forceps and cut them off, then treat as described until they are healed, and be wary of cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must treat the sutures in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then draw the thread from above and make the needle pierce from another side, and twist both ends of the thread under the needle, and let them be wide; then tightly pull the thread, then tie the knot, remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain excess blood; then place a moistened piece of cloth in rose oil or cerate on the foundation, and place it over the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; then leave it until they fall off, and when they have fallen off, treat them with ointment and other remedies, until he is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the bowels or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is constipation of feces in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut with the point of a spatula or your fingernail into the surface, without allowing it to become moistened; then treat it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot be dried, then shave it more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much, and becomes scabbed over; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small scabby appearance on the body, and it spreads very quickly; and sometimes it is found in cold areas, and one feels it like being dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the whole body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose’s feather or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill on the boil so that the circles perfectly surround the boil; then turn your hand around the entire quill until you cut all around the boil, and place it properly, and scrape out the boil from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be fine underneath and drawn over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the threads in place and to press them. And if you wish, cauterize the boil as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or sorrel, or of molten silk or barley; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to the needs of those who receive them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who administer treatment to children and those who are weak and in pain use small instruments.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is as follows, and the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a space where the belly is bound as you see, and the end inside should be perforated; it should have two holes on one side and one on the other; and the belly into which the medicine is placed should be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and should be perforated all around with small holes, and there should be a space of one finger between each hole, then insert a strong thread through these holes in a helical manner, and secure the belly as if it were a drum; when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread beforehand, then administer the enema; this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a douche of oil or oak bark, or something similar, then pour it on gently; then spread the patient's fingers in both hands together until they are fully open, then remove the douche, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer an enema in a case of diarrhea and the medicine comes out quickly, repeat it until it stays.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or an abscess, then the enema should be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema in which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the section the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments and medicines according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from falling stones and cuts from swords, knives, lances, staves, arrows, or similar objects; they are made in different parts of the body, such as a wound on the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, and other limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple head wounds, because memory will come into its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from falling of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound large, and you doubt the development of hot abscess: then I make it immediately heal with cephalic treatment directly if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the dressing be contrary to the injured part; and avoid the patient overloading on wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal it, then reduce his meat intake, and let him drink no wine nor eat flesh; and put on the wound, should hot abscesses come, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the fresh wound that has not been exposed to air, powder which I will describe a little later; and if it has become irritated by exposure, then apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the edges cannot be brought together by tents, then sew them together as I will say about belly wounds, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone, and it is flabby, and only holds together at one point, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, such as brains and boiled wheat, as well as porridge, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrid skin in the wound that adheres not to the bone, then cut out all the putrefaction and apply a poultice, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched with medicines, tie off the artery; and if you find it dislocated, ligature it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
