Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light; it consists of applying this powder that seals as though the wound has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of quicksilver, and mix the powder finely, then apply it to the wound, and press it firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, and do not loosen it if it does not swell; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses quicksilver alone when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the wound must not be allowed to close.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in winter, do not apply this powder; but put on some digestible ointments, or make a poultice of barley flour with water and honey until it runs fluid; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, then there is no other remedy but to leave the treatment alone and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water washed in sweet water, and rose oil mixed likewise in sweet water, and copper leaf washed similarly in sweet water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and ligature with bandages, then treat it until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, then incise them at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then stop it, ligature it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the esophagus, and the path for food is blocked, then sew the esophagus onto the cartilage of the throat, but do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural position; and then bind it carefully, and leave it alone for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until he is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then curette it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot have, let them be as long as the wound heals and becomes disinfected; and if the wound is fresh, then apply the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, then check if there is air swelling in the wound where the patient's breath goes: you will know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, but fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it at first hour, nor bind it because of the blood that does not clot deeply, and return to the heart, killing the patient; instead apply a drawing ointment, and bandage it twice a day. If you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will be no spasms, nor bad heart tremors, foreign objects intruding; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with bandages and other treatments until he is healed; and if she cannot heal him, and you work on it, then know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it accordingly; if it is large, sew it up; and if it is small, powder it; and if it is pressed into the bone, with pieces chipped off, then clean the wound, and remove any protruding fibers if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound drain, which will ease the extraction; and judgments for other wounds on other limbs are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, which requires an internal examination; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if you do not place the intestines back immediately, they swell quickly upon feeling the cold, and thus enter less easily, and for this reason a smaller rupture is better, since you can more easily return the intestine to its place compared to other wounds. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: two common sutures occur with abdominal surgery, and the suturing of other body wounds are similar but distinct; yet they are more specific to abdominal surgeries, and I will explain each one separately and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines protrudes, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a piece of linen in hot water only, which you cook with vinegar and rue and spikenard, and rinse the intestines until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use wine that constricts to do so, and it should be mild enough to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water in which aloes and mallows have been cooked, for this gradually opens the entry; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be such that one does not need to cut unless there is great necessity; and here is the instrument for making the incision: cut inward along the curvature but do not go outwards, and you will see its form here.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, put them back in place according to their natural form if you have the power, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the front part of the belly, raise his head and feet higher than the middle parts; and similarly, if a rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, place your attention so that the wounded part is raised higher than the other; and thus you must treat what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, apply what is appropriate to you, then have a needle ready in your hand that covers the entire wound and brings together the edges; this is the common method of stitching, and it involves taking one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving two fingers' breadth from the beginning of the wound, and inserting a strong thread through the needle at that point; then pierce both sides of the skin with the inner side of the siphac tissue, so that you pierce it throughout this part, and bring together the four edges; then strain a double thread around the needle on both sides, then join the two edges of the wound gradually, leaving two fingers' breadth again, and insert another needle there; tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to how many needles are needed until the entire wound is held together; the needles should be medium-sized between fine and coarse, because too fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter properly: therefore they should be medium-sized; it is also not advisable to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin as they may damage the wound before suturing; then trim the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and place bandages or cloth on the needle ends to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds. The second type of suture is common, and it involves bringing together both sides of the skin and both sides of the inner tissue at one needle with a medium-strong thread; when you have pierced all four edges thoroughly, reinsert the needle back where you started in the way clothes are sewn; leave a distance between each stitch as wide as a finger's breadth. This suture is well-known to people, and I stitched a wound that a man had on his abdomen which was cut by a knife, the wound being more than one handbreadth large, with intestines protruding two palm lengths, and it was located in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to him after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated him, and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old linen on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the thickness straight through, place the head of the suture where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part outwards; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do with fur, and leave once the suture on one side, and take it up on the other, until the entire suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: they join the two parts naturally together and bring one end of the suture to the other end in such a manner: pierce with a needle at the nearest point of the margin, piercing that place only, leaving both ends of the suture; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner part through both ends of the suture; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part in two other points of the margin on the opposite side; this is the most effective method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this and some people attest to it: one should stitch the belly with two needles, each having thread; and you must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the belly, the stitching is more difficult than for other areas of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the burn had moved it, place back the intestines and sew; then apply healing powder to the flesh, and if the burn has moved it, place any ointment that is present until the wound drinks; then stitch the wound, and let the edges be sealed together and the margins; then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on old cotton as soon as it begins to drink pus, twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members, it is necessary to moisten light wool in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and inside the armpits; and if pain or putrefaction occurs in the bowels, which often happens, then administer an enema of boiled black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the smallness of its veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would with the intestine while it is fresh; and if it has become old and blackened, then tie off the area that is black so that no more blood comes out, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligament, and let the two ends hang from below the wound until they dry up to facilitate extraction when the spleen falls out, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are punctured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be repaired in some people, for I saw a man pierced in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, from which excretion and flatulence came out; I applied treatment as best I could, and continued to suture until he was healed, and the tissue closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it closing, I feared the patient would have pain in his abdomen; but he had none, and remained in better condition, eating and drinking. And some experienced practitioners say that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be treated as follows: take clamps with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the clamp opens its mouth, place it on both sides so that it holds them together; then cut off the head, and this remains firm so that it cannot come loose, then place another clamp in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is covered; then sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head of the intestine is burned and causes no harm to the patient, then it can be tied with a thin thread that matches the intestine of an animal in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread and strip it bare, then wind a fine linen thread around its tip, put the thread on a needle, sew through the intestine, and pull it tight at the wound; and this method of stitching is no different from according to the path of trust and hope; if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the major intestines, there is no remedy or healing except for delicacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is covered and retracts inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to truth an abnormal swelling hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hairy like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it appears clear liquid, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, except for by one of the IX causes: to wit, because of the smallness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, near the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much liquid; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine used in treatment was not good; or because the corruption resembles pestilence; or due to the property in the region being slow digestion, and delayed healing, swollen by nature; or there are veins within the bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall instruct you on the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and some affect the principal part of the limb and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment, and wish to know it, take a probe made of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, then probe it; and if the fistula is curved, use a delicate probe made of lead, for lead can bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly explore it with probes, then inject through one of its openings, as moisture will flow from one opening to another, and clean it; then carefully press your hand to determine whether there is bone or nerve, and feel thoroughly, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press and where they feel it; once you truly know where it is, and if it is far from a joint, a nerve, an artery or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned, then treat it as I have said, and remove the diseased flesh inside; and continue to cure until it heals; and if the fistula is deeply straight, you must cut directly into it as much as possible, then place moistened probes with bitter medicine deep within, so that the excess matter at the bottom corrodes away; then apply healing ointments for new tissue until it is healed; and if it does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not trouble you in the principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat it until all the corruption is removed, then heal the flesh until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to its state before, know that you have not gone deep enough: uncover and seek until you are at the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy than leaving it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can pull with forceps, then extract it with an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, pull them all out without leaving any; and if moisture impedes you, and there is neither error nor fear, cut away the flesh and let the bones be exposed.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, place over the wound something that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bone; then the bones will be more easily removed. And if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, cut away only the corruption until all the black matter is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupt part reaching to the marrow, you must scrape and cut it out completely up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened in a man's leg so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from something that came inside the body, such that the matter reached the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to let it burst; but due to the physicians' folly, they operated until the abscess opened and much matter flowed out, turning into a fistula, and many openings appeared through which all sorts of bodily fluids leaked. Many doctors treated him for two years without any success in their art, until I was called upon. Upon seeing his leg and the medicines used to treat it, as well as what was flowing from the openings into large quantities; his body had turned red and he had a yellowish complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set a tent in one of the holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered part of the bone, and found it corrupt and perforated, with corruption reaching to the bone inside; I treated what appeared to be the corrupted bone, thinking there was no further corruption beyond that which I removed; and began to heal the wound with astringent medicines over a long time, but could not close it; then I started again, and cut into the bone as before, finding continuous corruption in the bone, which I treated and removed, and tried to close the place; but I was unable until I cut around one palm's width of the bone, down to its marrow, and then healed it with medicines; and it quickly became healthy and closed, except for needing further work due to the patient’s weakness, which could not endure, and out of fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often happens, but he was entirely healthy, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, and he was well disposed with no harm or contrary effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take some linen, and pull it at the end of the visible bone, and have someone stretch it upward; and place another thicker piece of flaxen cloth over the skin covering the bone, and extend the end so that you draw the corrupted flesh inward, and uncover the skin where you wish to treat, so that the dressing does not hurt the skin; and put a cautery or some wood under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh; and it is necessary to continue treating until corruption can be seen and felt, and treat again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place an ember underneath, and then cut across the corruption from one side to the other, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut off the corrupt joint, and sew up the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no remedy but cutting; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or foot, it is very strong that thing, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you; and clean it in all manners as you can, but let not the vein or nerve hinder you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare each kind of work its instrument; and know that your work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so think about the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or due to external factors; and when you have treated that corruption with the medicine, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from death by this means, or from the greater malice of losing the limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and rots afterwards, for the corruption spreads from limb to limb, and takes over the entire body; therefore hurry with amputation, and if it is due to a venomous animal bite, such as sea scorpion or wyrm and similar, if the corruption reaches the head of the arm, then cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, death is certain, and no remedy works except for its quantity of virtue; and do exactly this when the corruption reaches the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cover after the second joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut the entire foot; and if it ascends to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other means than letting the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you tie it from above and below, and one minister holds down one of the ligatures, and another minister holds up the other ligature, then cut apart the flesh between the two ligatures to a breadth of one span, until the bone is exposed; then cut or sew, and place a piece of linen on each side so that the wound does not touch healthy skin and cause the patient further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the area quickly or apply some powders that constrict; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my practice: he suffered from a blackness that seemed like a burn caused by fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot’s toe, spreading throughout the entire foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hurried to amputate his foot, and was healed; and after some time, the corruption returned to his hand’s thumb, and he came to me, and I applied substances that would repel the matter after purifying the body, but could not stop the corrosion; and he wished that I cut off his hand, which I did not want, hoping to repel the material; and I also feared that if I were to amputate his hand, he might die, for his constitution was weak; and he despaired completely, returned home, and hurried to amputate his hand, and was healed; and except for this case where another approach was taken when necessary, there is nothing more to say.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess occurs in the flesh and remains so long that it accumulates a large amount of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving the flesh behind, like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as fine cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut around all of that skin, and likewise when it is thin, like fine cloth; and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin will heal and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with a clister (enema) as follows: check if the breast is swollen, and the pus inside has an unpleasant odor, then administer an Egyptian medicine enema made thusly: take myrrh, oil, and litharge in equal parts, heat them in a vessel over fire until they turn red and become as thick as honey; then take this mixture according to your need and mix it with water and honey, then administer the breast enema, and squeeze the opening; let the medicine stay inside for two hours, then expel it gently; do this repeatedly until the breast is cleansed of its foulness; if the patient cannot tolerate it or the Egyptian medicine, use water from ashes instead; take ash from grapevine wood, pour water over it, filter it, and administer as an enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned. If neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water can be used, then administer an enema of honey and wine with a little litharge powder mixed in; or use an enema made from honey and vinegar where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash while the vinegar aids in healing. After doing this, if you trust that the breast is well cleansed, administer an enema that causes flesh to grow, such as using a poultice of diaphoretic herbs mixed with rose oil and wine; or use certain medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned when discussing ointments. If the opening in the breast is small, and the tube for the enema cannot enter, widen it slightly with an iron tool and apply a patch of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; if the wound is too large, sew around it leaving only one place where the enema can be administered, and if the pus-gushing hole is above, cut it lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, prepare in such a manner that the boil runs downward to the lowest place where it is. For when the boil is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate, and if you cannot cut the breast as you wish, prepare in such a way: that the boil flows slightly downwards, and leave nothing of the boil behind; then take consolidating medicines to put on the healthy tissue, and stretch a linen cloth covering all the healthy tissue; then cut at the strong points the hole in the breast somewhat larger than the first, then spread ointment under another piece of cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening in the flesh to ease the boil, and do not remove the large cloth for several days; and that which is on the opening of the breast, take often to remove the pus, and examine what comes from the boil, whether it is venomous or foul or moderate, or digested or undigested; and be wary if the patient feels pain or numbness, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in such a manner and you see the nature rising to the opening of the flesh, know that the healing has begun, and health approaches; then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons affect after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people for whom meat delays healing in their wounds, and others do the opposite; and if undigested food vomits from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if digestion is slow and prolonged, apply medicines that are dry in substance but moist in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the final remedy; prepare a diaphoretic ointment using rose oil, and rinse it with equal parts old wine; then thicken it and use it; and similarly, when diaphoretic ointments are not available, take murre, aloes, and incense, grind them together, mix them with honey on the fire; then spread a cloth dipped in this mixture over the stomach; sometimes administer aristonogogue longus and roots of celestial lilies, which resemble flour made from fennel and centaury; use these individually or as a compound: grind them into powder, add the honey I mentioned, and apply it; if the condition persists without improvement after treatment, then know that corruption is deep-seated, affecting bones, hard members, or ligaments; treat it with fistula cures as we have described previously.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises from under the nail of the hand or foot, or occasionally on other fingers; and when it ages and is not attended to, a painful abscess develops, spreading and pus flows until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly spreads completely; and corrosion comes up to the bone, causing severe pain, and the head of the finger becomes swollen, and its color changes.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and it begins to hurt, and becomes swollen, then you must place the blade under the nail that hurts the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away that flesh carefully and lightly, and put the remaining flesh on medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it away and draw out pus, for as long as the corrupted part of the bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone is corrupted, then cut it off at the joints as previously mentioned, then cure until it is healed; and if it is pierced and infected, and he feels great pain, then first cleanse it thoroughly; then carefully trim the nail with a sharp instrument by cutting across, and be careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the stiffness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bones, and at times there is a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birth is in some ways different for the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with any knot in the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may sometimes move; the size of one who is entirely flesh is so small, in this manner: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful when cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the rear end, you must first cut away the flesh roundly until reaching the bone, then cut the bone in a single stroke suitable for that person, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by inflammation of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut away that swelling so that the parts can be repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or moistened linens in rose oil so they do not swell again; or you may place between two pieces of fine cloth until the area is sealed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If firmly comes to any of his two with the palm, cut that soldering as it is appropriate.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick, swollen, filled with melancholic superfluities, which occur in many parts of the body; and this happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer enema cleansing at times, and then treat with basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron treatment is according to two methods: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment is as follows: first rise the leg with hot water very strong, until the thick blood becomes thin, then lift the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut a vein in one place, or two, or three, of a small size, then raise and draw out black blood to your hand, from one side to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can withstand; and then bandage it, and command him to feed on foods that cause black bile; and begin again the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and this benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of raising a vein is as follows: lift the patient's leg if there are many hairs, then place it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swells the veins; and if you do not have a bath, warm it by fire, then cut along the vein from the long part to the knee head, or at the part below the ankle; then work the skin with an awl and scrape the vein on each side until it feels rough when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then raise it underneath, as you have done, and smooth it with another awl, as you did before; then cut another incision or more if needed, then lift it and cut at the toe joint, then draw it out and lift it to the second incision; then pull out vein by vein until all is drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle along one strong double thread, tie and pull, place another underneath, and move your hand back and forth until it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, which is harmful to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, put wet wool in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and treat it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not sever it; and draw it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the knife used to cut the vein is curved and does not have sharp edges so that it does not cut the vein; it has a broad curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground with little moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it arises within the body like serpents and worms, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the location changes, and the vein begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap it around a piece of linen from one and a half to two fingers' width, tie it securely, and let the linen hang down the leg. Every time there is a point where it starts to pull away, wrap it around the linen again and tie it; if it is too long, cut part of it but do not cut it at its root until it has all come out completely; because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh causing an abscess or corruption in that place leading to a bad illness. For this reason, it must be treated bit by bit until there is nothing left on the body; and sometimes this vein when treated is as long as five palms, or ten, and once upon a time it came out twenty inches for me, issuing from a length of ten palms, and when you cut it, it spews forth one row or hole, and pierce it all the way through so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside, and treat the place with medicines to heal corruption for some days, then cure it as is done with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is deeper, especially when it appears in the ankle joint, or at the foot, and there is much perforation, and from which it bleeds heavily; treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "the cattle disease," because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it penetrates the skin where it goes, causing pain; and it arises from putridity of certain humors, such as when worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids come from the belly; and there is fear of its malice, because as it travels through the body, if it ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, by chance it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it needs to be opened and drained, one cannot do so forcefully: therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut over it and drain it forcefully; if the pus is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies down; and the greatest harm it causes is that it can corrupt the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching near the eye, hold firmly below the eyebrow, then cut over it, and drain it forcefully; and the patient must use purgative medicines to clear bad humors and avoid consuming foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from gas or windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.
