I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a short while later spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it kept circling around her body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have often heard that some wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought this was because the woman had a dry body, and veins exposed, so this windiness appeared constrained; and they do not appear according to this reason for those who are fat, and who have moist bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you want to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, lift it above and below quickly, and then apply heat until that windiness is constrained at its place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your eyes, cure it through those who expel winds, such as fetid pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small points, barbed points, and fixed points; and those with two angles, and some with tongues, and others with pieces; and when an arrow strikes any limb, it does so in two ways: either striking a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes any part of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you next, become apparent: then you must be wary about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many circumstances; and when such bad signs do not appear and the arrow is not deeply embedded, extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow hits and pierces the bone, and penetrates the dura mater which is over the brain, is when there is scotoma and coma and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and by chance it issues without strength from the nostrils, or ears; and by chance loses speech and voice; and flows from the wound white moisture like pus, and also as a stream of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then hold yourself ready for treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it hits the heart is that it is near the left mammary region, and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not an empty one; and by chance the arrow moves like pus, and forms black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope occurs: you then know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that wounds the throat is that without much foam blood spouts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls in the cover of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and he throws up a large quantity of phlegm and suffers great pain and sighs; and all his shoulder members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, by chance something of undigested food may spurt from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and no sign of it can be found through the intestines, there is no hope for healing, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to leak, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and joint and spine of the back and forearm and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, do as I say.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell in his helmet at the root of his nose: I examined it, and extracted it from the other side under the ear fat, and he was safe without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he pulled out an arrow that had struck the fat of the eye below the membrane below, and the arrow was buried, and barely could they reach but the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large for a Turkish bow, made entirely of light iron without barbs; the patient was safe, and no ill accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with barbs: I seized the barbs, and carefully extracted it, and the Christian was safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he pulled an arrow from the man who had it embedded in his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I cut around the arrow, probed it, forcefully extracted it, and he suffered no ill consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change any of his natural dispositions, nor finds harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man who has an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is sealed over; and it remains thus without him suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow in the head of one of the king's princes, which was embedded between his ears, and it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely bent. I was called for treatment three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it thoroughly with great care, and felt nothing; yet he experienced pain and soreness behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a poultice that prevents swelling to the area, so as not to allow the place around the arrow to swell; and the spot where the arrow was became visible.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several more days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained in this condition for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose one day; and then he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and then examined it, feeling the tip of the arrow lodged in the spot; I continued to apply this medicine around the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became visible; after about four months, I opened the wound so widely that I could fit pincers inside, but it would not come out; therefore, I did not stop trying and inventing various instruments until one day I was able to grasp it with well-made pincers, as described at the end of this chapter, and then removed the arrowhead and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I repaired it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so place your care on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters compare well with great things, and with what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit from the members where they are lodged in two ways: either at the place where they enter, or from another part; and those that come out through the place where they entered are penetrating arrows, and sometimes come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the surrounding flesh is putrefied and the opening enlarged; and also if it is embedded in the bone and cannot be removed, leave it thus for several days, and soften it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, perforate around with a very fine point until the flesh around it is widened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned become apparent to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it for several days until it is even, because if the arrow reaches the brain tissue, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for several days without any adverse event, then devise how to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, administer terebinth around it, as I told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a place on the body where it cannot be seen, search throughout the tent for it; and if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, cut until the wound is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has grooves by which it holds fast, remove the flesh that is embedded on both sides as much as possible, then break or bend the grooves so you may extract it; be careful not to break the arrow, making extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the area around the site is healed, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then treat it as we have said in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and place a guide so that you may draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot, then place him as the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it reveals some part of itself, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly: cut then above it until pliers can grasp it, and then extract it; now do so immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push with all of the shaft; and if the shaft breaks, and you wish to administer a probe, use an instrument head so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push firmly, and if the arrow is stuck, use an instrument with a sharp end to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the wound is, if you can, and then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or in the belly or bladder or in the side, and it is near, and you can cut above it; be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary; treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the piercing needle is also like the quill of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for inserting and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed to become healthy, sixteen of which are in the head: two large ones behind the ears, called the "herbech"; and the two arteries visible in the temples; and the two veins in the tear ducts of each eye, called "aspires"; the vein on the forehead; the vein at the top of the nose; the two jugular veins in the neck; and the two veins under the upper lip, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one usually draws blood are four in each arm: the first is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the left side, and the barber people call this "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste," and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the barber people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it the "vein of the belly," and it runs along the ulnar bone, and this is the vein from which one usually draws blood, which appears clearly on the arm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and on the foot are three veins: one is below the bend of the left arm vein, and the second sophene which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse," which is at the other ankle; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The salve applied to the veins behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraines; and concerning the properties of this salve, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient’s neck with a bandage such that the two veins become visible behind the ears in two places: press them with your thumb at these spots, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, incise there; then take the lancet and puncture beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut through both the skin and the vein well twice its width, letting out as much blood as you wish; then bind it tightly until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the two temples is valuable for treating chronic migraine, severe headache, habitual ophthalmia, and persistent tears in the eyes; and the qualities of this bloodletting are as I say: it is that the patient compresses his neck until the two veins become clearly visible; then feel the pulse below your thumb, and afterwards open the vein with a lancet; lift the vein upwards on your finger above, place the lancette underneath, and raise the vein up, and cut it, just as you did in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to necessity; then release the patient, and put the hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; afterwards tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; we have also spoken about their coagulation and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for treating old face diseases and headaches; and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein appears swollen; then take the instrument called "digger", which here is its form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you desire; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healthy; sometimes one performs this work with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp; and the incision should be sideways, because the bone is close, and by chance the flame might break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The salve of the two veins that are in the two canthi helps with the eyes, and for tinea, and redness, and ulceration in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their salve is that the patient strains his neck by twisting some ligament as before; then applies the salve, and let it be made thick, a little long like a flame a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are fine, it may break; then let blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cloth, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The salve of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for violent sores, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the salve is that the patient strains his neck, then pinches his nose with your left hand, and take a fine long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not appear well inside, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, for it restores quickly; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two binders helps in the tightening of the groin, and at the beginning of mixing, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosions, and herpes, and esthiomenes; and the quality of the salve is that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then apply the vein from the long slightly widely, then draw some tempered blood, as much as needed; then treat similarly in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and tighten all veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve for the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The salve for the veins of the lips above helps with sores in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and splits in the lips, and nostrils, and around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the salve are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their black color, and by the small black veins around them: so cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and likewise do for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Remove the tongue from the socket
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The surgery of the veins that are behind the tongue follows the surgery of the cephalic area, which is at the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the surgeon are such that the patient urinates into your hands towards the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look underneath on each side there is a black vein: therefore treat one and the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated are operated on according to two methods: either by cutting with a broad flame-shaped blade, or with an olive-shaped fine blade like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire flame is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and is used to treat fine veins, where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the abdomen; and it is necessary for the physician to bleed carefully, and to avoid the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood begins to flow out, it must be staunched, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with a flame but cut as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, then you must separate it and change another one; or take a little from it, or open the vein in its place on the arm: it appears clearly; and cut with a flame as before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the puncture, then it is necessary for you to separate the arm, touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot on the bone, and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a flame as before; and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the area swollen, because that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is arterial blood: hurry then, and place your hand lengthwise, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it affects you, and no medicine is present, then cut the artery if it appears, for its end can be found; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take the bark of a fig tree, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the bandaging should not be difficult in many positions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the binding of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps by drawing blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to protect himself behind the nerve that lies underneath, and if he pricks too deeply and finds the nerve, it swells and his hand becomes paralyzed, and perhaps he cannot operate anymore; and this nerve appears very often, and if it does not appear in some people because of its subtlety, then you must heal it with anesthetic instruments; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps by drawing blood from the head and assists the eyes; and it is necessary to operate on it by making an incision in the olive branch or the myrtus branch, because it is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to choose the most gentle spot, and do not cause any pain even if it must be done for the first time, and one can repeat; and by chance, the area may swell in some people when it is done for the first time, but it does not cause any pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should not be done except to maintain health and to prevent future diseases; and one should bleed in one of the three veins which are on the arm: namely, cephalic, basilic, and median; and bleeding should occur at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear; and it is best to perform bloodletting on the first or third day, two or three hours after dawn.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who treats diseases has no fixed time for treatment, but whenever the need arises day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it is not right to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not treat the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, they should cleanse their intestines with a gentle enema if there is much retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful excesses from the intestines; and one does not bleed those who are too full of food, nor drunkards, whether male or female, until they have sobered up, nor hydropics. Do not bleed after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive sexual activity, labor, staying awake, fasting, or anything that exhausts the body by deed or substance; then carefully purify the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines if you have the skill. Then enter a bath, unless something prevents it, to refine the blood; then bleed from the vein of your choice near the third hour as we have said; and keep yourself free of work, pain, lust, and similar things that day; be happy and joyful, and let the barber stand higher than the person being bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then loosen the binding moderately because if it is too tight, the blood cannot flow freely. Then feel the vein with your hand until you can see them swelling and feel their pulse; then moisten the lancet tip with a little old oil, place your left hand over the intended bleeding site, so that the vein does not rise when pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like strings to the surgeon, and some of them are full of airiness, so when one applies flame, it draws back from the flame, and thus one cannot open the vein; and if one works on the vein, the wound is too narrow. Therefore, it is necessary for surgeons to be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened the first time, it is good; if not, then start again a bit below that place quickly, provided the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps a soft abscess will come; nor enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, apply the flame directly to that opening quickly, so that the area becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen it again, and put a poultice of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this spot the poultice of oil is soothing; and thus administer the poultice of oil each time you treat the veins to stop the flow of blood; and also make triacle and apply it when you place it on the spot; it delicately thins the blood when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the treatment of veins is not frequent enough or when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and place on the spot a sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar for a little while; and it must be done after the blood flows from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains at the site after several days, it does no harm; and if you wish, apply something of aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mastix, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and swelling occur at the base of the thumb: put your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft upon pressing with your hand, then that swelling is harmful.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything of what we have said above, for it may cut into the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat with another method until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out the blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too warm, allow it to cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for the one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, make a wider incision, and let the flaps be wide; and for the weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed them gently and frequently, and one should bleed them by cutting diagonally, not vertically; and this method of bleeding prevents loss of blood and injury to nerves, and is worth more than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose body needs nourishment before bleeding, give him moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, let him bleed three or four times. And if he has a cold constitution, let him eat moistened bread in musé syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup before bleeding.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing a lot of blood, then it is necessary that he drink broth made of meat, and aromatic syrup, and use other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and be bled again, then when he is weakened by excessive bleeding, it is necessary that he be bled a little at a time according to the quantity of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another site should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; so it must be drawn in large quantities, and widen the passage until it flows freely; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions for safety, place your hand upon the pulse as it bleeds, lest death come to the patient's aid, which often happens when barbers are negligent; nor should you press firmly when you wish to release the arm a second time, and the passage is closed; nor if it is curved, extend the arm quickly, for that would be worse; but leave it until it bleeds freely the second time; or prick with the tip of flame, until the blood which has congealed in the vein's opening issues forth, and place a small poultice wetted in water on it, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not bind it, until the abscess is alleviated.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is well-composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until it turns red; then wrap moderately so that the vein appears clearly, and bleed now through its width, not lengthwise or crosswise; make the punctures wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, put the hand back in warm water again, and let the blood run freely in the water until you have enough; and if this is done in summer, do not bathe the hand in warm water more than necessary, for it should be done more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins because there are no arteries or nerves nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salvation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: pull out the hand, and put it in hot water, until the veins are swollen, if one can see them; and if the salve crosses, and if you cut it through entirely, it does not harm anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are under completely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and no blood can come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and wax to seal the vein quickly, and do this for each incision.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do it exactly as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophene is worth for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the legs, retention of urine, disease of the thighs, and old diseases of the calves and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the patient immerses their foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it breaks, and ties it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there flow many veins; apply it then to the largest vein, or at the ankle, for that is most effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it to the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and apply it across as if cutting; and let the flame be calm.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, place the foot in warm water, and let the vein be opened well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision is necessary the first time, do it slightly higher for the second time, as the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and thus do the same incision on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site for the sciatic vein is at the ankle on the side, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its incision is such that the patient enters the bath, and applies pressure above the ankle for IV digits by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it does appear, incise it in all ways you can, including crosswise; and beware that you do not cut it short, as the site is deep, and it responds well to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then apply a poultice to the spot on the back of the foot near the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; let the blood flow as much as you wish, then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on and bind it tight; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	suction treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping instruments are made of horns, or wool, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by drawing blood or without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without drawing blood is done in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves drawing blood and extracting blood is performed at fourteen locations on the body, of which one is at the top of the head; another is around the neck; two are on each side of the neck; there is a cupping spot under the chin; and cuppings for both shoulders; and cuppings above the kidneys; and cuppings in the arms; and cuppings on the legs; and cuppings on the ankles; and this type of cupping does not draw much blood, only from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and thus it does not weaken a person as bleeding from a vein would; and it should not be administered with heat or without heat in any disease caused by congestion, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to use cupping, or by habit, we bring this each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are such people who, when they need cupping, feel a heavy head; and there are those who experience bloating and redness on their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who see drops of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongues, and cough up blood; and there are some who dream, seeing by night blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we instruct them to undergo cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The massage of the temples helps with headaches that come from the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is instead in place of the cephalic massage, and it is not suitable for those who have a cold constitution to use it, or who suffer from catarrh, as it causes them great harm; and therefore it is not appropriate for elderly people to use it, nor for those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become too relaxed from it may become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a bit lower out of fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of head massage and basilic treatment, and it is useful for tightness in the chest, rib fractures, coughing, and congestion; and it should be done gently, because if it holds too firmly, it may cause forgetfulness or discomfort in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosation between the two ribs of the neck is effective for headaches, ophthalmia and migraine, and in cases of choking, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is located at the site of the basilica's treatment; and you must instruct the healer that he should press his hand gently when applying it, so as not to cut the artery, nor cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosation below the chin is effective for mouth diseases, and gum infections, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is located at the site of the treatments of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosation of the shoulders is effective for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The venesection of the arms is worth as much as that of three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the doctor not to cut too deep, for the flesh there is thin, and near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venesection on the buttocks is equivalent to hemorrhoids of the anus and diseases beneath it, and it should be large, made of brass, as it needs to draw blood well; and if it were delicate, it might break; and thus it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesections of the legs are very effective, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are useful for treating chronic pains in the thighs, and of the joints, and of the bladder, and reset the flowers; and they are performed at two sites on the shins, and on the ankles, and over time they weaken the body, and can lead to fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the cupping vessel is to place it first empty, then temper it, and put it quickly, moving it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then apply heat, and replace the cups, and take care in the condition of the body, for there are some who have thin flesh, and clear pores: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to make the blood flow more freely.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out the blood little by little, we do it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we lose a lot of blood, we often restart it; and if the blood is thick, then apply force, and the ends should be such that the wound is pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick skin and hard, narrow pores, you should anoint the areas with suction cups using an oil that is stimulating and dissolving: if this is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is winter, use cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then use marjoram oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to whom treatment is given has tender skin and large pores, it is not necessary to apply any oil, but they should be washed after ventosity with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should rise from a bath of myrtle water, or sumac water, or similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or larch water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar; and it is not appropriate to bleed with a ventouse before the bath nor in the bath, but one hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after the ventosity, and it is necessary for them to walk when they should be ventosed and when they are ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch if the person who is bleeding has a choleric temperament, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as sour apples and endives and lettuce in moderation, and similar things; and eat young birds, and castrated meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and wine that is between old and new, and eat pigeon, and young birds and small birds and doves; and on the day they will be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and some people should sometimes be given triacle or nutmeg before bleeding, or after, to comfort the principal limbs; and the blood should be subtle, but it is not appropriate for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and for gout, and on the abdomen and buttocks and thighs and hip, because these members do not tolerate being cut on them, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we place suction cups on the breasts when the veins are congested; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we apply suction cups on the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the swelling; and they alleviate pain where there is obstruction or stone, removing it through their attractive power perhaps from its place; and similarly, they act when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained gas, these suction cups are administered empty for suctioning only; sometimes they are administered together with heat, and at times filled with tepid water, as in cases of pleurisy, and likewise filling the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.
