And it has two digits wide and half a palm thick, and on the side there is a small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron for holding a candle, and they come in different sizes according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for cupping vessels for children are different from those for elderly people, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping vessel on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or linen and insert it into the cupping vessel through the crossbar inside it, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping vessel to prevent it from burning the patient; then place the cupping vessel on the limb, with the opening being the small hole we mentioned earlier, so that when you want to do so, the vapor goes in and removes the cupping vessel; then take out the linen as before, and repeat this often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment used for pleurisy, in all acute cases, there is no rod or hole, and it is not applied except when it is full of blood, and it is placed only on the limb; and this is the method:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are used only in parts where cups cannot be applied due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas; and in exposed flesh areas, such as the hands or feet, and other similar places; and the quality of use is that when you find cupping glasses that are in mild cases clean and ready for treatment, take them; put one nut in a mild liquid until they become familiar and have nothing inside; then let it be treated with vein opening and cupping, rub the limb until it becomes red, and place the cupping glasses on it; when they are full and fall off, if it is an area where cups can be applied, apply them, because this is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the place of rest, and then with water, very well, and then press it; and if the wound heals too quickly over the flesh without opening, soak a linen cloth in cold water and apply it until the blood is absorbed; and if the blood is excessive, apply ground vitriol or gallnut powder, or similar things, until it is absorbed; or place half a pound of shelled beans on the wound and leave them there until they dry up, now it will stop; and if you need more remedies, take other plasters.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the plasters do not want to take hold, rub the wound with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the blood comes out, and then apply the plasters, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see them falling off, sprinkle a little aloes and burnt frankincense powder, or ash, and now they will fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish doctors fall from this chapter because they have never seen any of the ancient books or read a single letter in them; and for this reason science is strange in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have clearly described in this chapter what is contained within it, and have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to treat the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, old people; or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cold things, that is to say cold broth, and meat of birds and kid, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot abscess, or spreading of matter in the limb; if the patient returns to soundness first from this governance which you have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause thick nourishment, which are viscous, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, heads and feet of animals, belly of fish, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment promotes healing and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit do not heal well or mend according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but pay no heed, reset the broken bone with a thick plaster that adheres and joins the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not remove any part of its work, and for this one must nourish with heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the hip, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, like the shaft of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its treatment and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory brings forth; and the fracture of the bone is known by its being twisted, and it is clearly evident by swelling, and sounds hollow when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it with your hand, but place the medicines that follow hereafter, and then gently press it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and where the two parts are disjoined, they must now be placed equally, so that no heat comes to it like in abscesses; and if a warm abscess does come to it, let him leave it for some days until the swelling subsides; then place it equal to what you can gently and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is easier than that where there are pieces; then press it as it should be done hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone with pieces broken, it is held by two parts, whether for hand or foot, or by one hand for a small member, or by two strings, or by one string and your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the fractured member are separated, you realign all additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then set it properly, and do not pull it too hard, nor press it as those do who make hot abscesses and limb contractions through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is securely positioned so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not properly set, and you must put it in such a position that it does not feel any pain; and be careful that it is placed correctly so that no curvature occurs when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands: they should be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: should be wrapped with wide and firm bandages, because the wide bandages embrace the entire limb, and compress it evenly, so there is no indentation; then tie around small rolls of cloth three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all the bandage, then go above the break and compress less, so that the break can move slightly away from the break; and loosen the bandage little by little, until you take in most of the healthy part, then start another layer, and wrap around again over the broken area; then retighten below the break moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first chapter above; then place between the bandages rolls of linen or cloths so that they are all even, then tie everything with a wide strip, and then put your well-made splints on if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing hot poultice for the abscess and to reduce the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then incise over your splints, which should be half the width of a palm thick, or made from wood used to make clives, or from strips of palm leaves, and they should follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint placed over the fracture be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as is appropriate for the limb, whether small or large; then incise over the splints as you did in the first dressing, then wrap a thread around them, just as was done in the first dressing on the fracture; the tighter above, the looser below; and it is necessary that the threads be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen; for if the threads are too thick, like those fools who make their dressings with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, because the dressing cannot be even if it is too fine, and it must not have less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the points of stakes after they are driven into their flesh, place cotton plugs or linen strips beneath them so that they do not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breacher, and the bone is broken, I will tell the treatment for it hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract stakes from all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to place stakes except after five days or seven, or more depending on your judgment of a hot abscess that might occur; and here you see the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour from the walls of the mill, mix it abundantly with eggs, apply this preparation neither too thick nor too thin, and use it; this is the common method of a plaster for healing fractures in various conditions, especially for women and children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take З of abares and storax and enule and asafoetida and gum arabic and mastic, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; and make powder, and mix with honey and egg yolk; if the person's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is well composed, and quickly restores broken bones, and suits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a plaster for twists: take mastic and bistort, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bole X З., and grind well, and mix with water or egg yolk, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones out of place, and to ease the pain arising, and the use of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and boil it in oil, and apply it to the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly relieves the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster to heal broken bones: take dried mulberry leaves and herb petals, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vervain, chamomile, violets, flour of oats, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vervain, seeds of flax, rosemary, hellebore, and pennyroyal, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply anything to a broken limb for restoration other than cerotic made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that for restoring a broken limb, dry and somewhat warm things should be applied, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make an ointment that is good for injuries and pain: take mutton suet, hair of men's head, feathers of birds, and vervain, in equal parts, grind them together, and make an ointment with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he loosens it a little after, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has moved the bone from its place; do not loosen by hand for several days. And if pain comes to the spot, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry up and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take fine linen, and sponge of sea water moistened, and plunge in water, and lift the area until the itching ceases, and the pain is eased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it over a bandage, until you are sure there will be no hot abscess; and ease the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle plastering, and a little plaster, but do not press so hard as before; and cautiously until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is reddened and painful and swollen has been removed from all sides, and you need ointment and linen, then begin again as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing happens to the limb as we have said, do not release it before III days or IIII or V or VII; and sometimes leave it for XX days, according to what you see, until the swelling subsides, and the edges of the wound heal; then bind it tighter than before, and fatten up the flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the area dries more than necessary, understand that no new tissue will form; soak it then with warm water whenever you release it, every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; thus prevents new tissue from forming in the limb, and improves quickly what the foolish doctors do wrongly: they rush to restore movement to the limb. This is harmful, and such practices are fearful, and I see nothing other than patience and proper treatment.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures made by sword strikes, where the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the surface that is beneath the bone, like splitting a staff or pole; and for this kind of fracture it is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a crack from falling on stone, or other similar incidents.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches as far as the membrane beneath the bone, whether it is on top of or underneath the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "hairline" fracture; and if the wound is made by being hit with a stone, or falling, or something similar, causing a piece of the bone to break inward, and the place where it breaks resembles how blacksmiths shape metal when they work on pots; then a piece of the bone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their head, such as the head of a child; and in all these types of fractures, small pieces are broken off like splinters; and I will speak about it at its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all manners of fractures by the depression above them, and through examination with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known by this: when the bone has been exposed and rubbed over it, the fracture appears clearly black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be mindful of the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, convulsions, cold sweats, intermittent fever, and eyes protruding and reddening, along with other similar conditions in many cases, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the injury that you may.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become corrupted, and avoid the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the fractured part as follows: take the head of the wounded person and expose the bone in every way that you can, and around the shape of the wound as deep as you can, and if blood flows from the opening of the wound or a dangerous abscess occurs, provide appropriate assistance, which involves filling the area with cloths soaked in rose oil; then allow the wound to rest until the dangerous abscess is calmed and bleeding has stopped; then begin removing around the bone according to two methods of work: one method is to cut narrowly ahead, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the second cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is to have various cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with pointed tips, made of iron; and work gently so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it, administering cuts with chisels, but not so deeply that they penetrate beyond the skull bone, and the tip should have a margin or circle to prevent the point from going through the bone; and you need several of these, each placed in its proper position on the skull; and this is the form of the third type of chisel:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one point on the bone and turn it until you know the bone is pierced; then move the point a little way off and do this all around, then with your incisors cut out the space of the bone between the holes, and do this as finely and lightly as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand or with any tools that you have such as pincers, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to remove any remaining tightness that adheres to the bone with another tool similar to an incisor, but it must be more blunt and finer than the other incisor; and if there remains anything of small bones or scales, remove them lightly with your tools; then treat the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen says, who is more skilled; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is apparent, so that when you have uncovered this part, you place underneath the head of this knife-shaped instrument, which has the following form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is beveled on two sides, so that the cutting edge faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet, so that you cut lightly around the entire bone, and take great care of the tissue beneath; if it is adhering to the bone, remove it gently, as it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut from above, with small pieces, then it is necessary behind that roughness, to remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various quantities, to adapt appropriately for each place according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large scrapers and then use finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and fine fractures, you must adapt according to their direction; and this is something that cannot be taught to one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the scalp is exposed, then you must take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another double layer of cloth and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first piece of cloth; do this as gently as possible so that you do not burden the scalp, then cover it with another bandage, but do not tighten it more than necessary to hold the dressing in place; leave it like this for one or two days until the swelling subsides, then remove it and apply medicines such as lily root, wheat flour, powdered frankincense, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder of these substances and apply it to the wound, and immediately administer cleansing medicines without causing irritation; and be careful that the wound remains clean so that you do not leave any ointment on it or allow pus to accumulate, for when pus forms over the membrane covering the brain, it can cause severe damage to the patient; because when something irritating is applied to the scalp, it can penetrate through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed if any harmful accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness appears other than from the medicine that has been applied, which may have such an effect, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil, mix them well, and apply it to the surface; then treat it according to appropriate methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or only one part, because they are two bones; and the lower one is made of cartilage, which does not break but may be pushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your small probe or needle into the anus, and align that break within your index finger, and outside with the pouch, until the anus returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the anus and your finger cannot reach the place, then you must align it along a probe slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do as described, and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after seven or ten days when the abscess has subsided, then insert into the head of the anus patches of linen if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you insert one from the other side, if there is a fracture; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the passages of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some physicians say that the tents should be moistened with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is right, but they should be moistened with a mixture of almond and egg, and powdered millet; then leave the tent in place until the bone is set, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one inserts goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is any inflammation around, and the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through them; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses occur in the nose while you are working on them, apply cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or a bit of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscesses occur, apply a plaster from behind made of linseed meal and powdered incense, cooked with some egg white, then place light plugs, but do not tie up the nose; and if there is a small fracture in the nose, broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then suture the fissure, and cure with substances that generate flesh and close wounds, such as plasters and ointments appropriate for this purpose; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and place strips of wax until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from below, and there is no wound to bleed from, and the breakage is only superficial, and it is not broken in two pieces, except for a small crack inside, one can easily recognize this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then insert your right index finger, gently push the fracture inward, and support it from the outside with the other hand, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is displaced in two parts, you must administer an extension of both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then pull them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place on the broken mandible wax, and put on two cloths; and place on the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and bind it securely as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day and then adjust what has changed; and apply a plaster with mill powder mixed with plenty of eggs or ground cumin after removing the wax; and place light wool over the plaster, and if the plasters stick and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is well; many times he is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if small abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to heal flesh, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks multiple times in front of the shoulder, and there are three types of fractures: where it is broken into two pieces but not displaced, which is easier to heal; where there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other to extend the neck towards the affected part; then set the fracture with your hands so that its form is as it should be, and there are no signs of displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, and make it as large as necessary; then extend and lift the collarbone, and hold the ball with your hand so that you can set the fracture properly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus out due to its position, then the patient should lie supine on his back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and push the shoulder down by the minister, until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, you must cut into it; gently pull apart the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any elevation, cut it with one of your incisors; but place this instrument under the humerus to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon and is not bristled, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and let it have two edges, as you see, one broad and the other narrow, like the outline of the wound you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the outline is small where you suspect a hot abscess, pad the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if painful abscesses come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and egg yolk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of a bone fracture, whether it involves cuts or incisions, is that you place the bone with the plaster made from mill powder and egg whites, and put light wool over it; if necessary, place a small ball under the joint. Then take a very wide bandage about one palm in width, place the double cloth and plaster on top of the wool; then take a fine stick three fingers wide and long, wrap the bandage around so that its ends hang down; place the stick over the fracture site, and roll the bandage around the neck, under the healthy joint, and under the affected one. Tighten it from each side, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture properly, and clearly that the stick does not move off the bone, check it daily, and when the ligaments loosen, re-tighten them; have the patient lie on their back, place a small pillow under the joint at night to lift the shoulder up; this will lighten the force of the fracture by elevating the shoulder, and you bind the arm to the neck for twenty days; then restart the plaster if necessary, keep it tight until it is healed; she is restored in about 28 days or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Rarely does the shoulder break either wide or in the middle, and one can only feel it by touch; thus, treat it according to the appearance of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways possible. Then place powder from the mill with an abundance of eggs, and use light bandages, and put on two layers of cloth; then place a wide and fine pillow, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if any part of the pillow is uneven where it touches the shoulder, stuff that area with linen bandages so that the pillow lies evenly. Then bind it tightly with a broad strip of cloth so that the pillow does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten it again, and make sure the pillow remains even if it shifts out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in twenty or twenty-five days. When this period is completed, release it carefully, for it is not a bone that resets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and points away from the heart, then cut it off, and do as we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to ease a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes fractured in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the side.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it leans to the side, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks appetite, and thirsts, and may vomit blood, and the movement of the bones can be felt clearly through the skin.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and carefully align it equally in all ways possible until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place poultices and dressings made of finely ground salt or other light material on top, and wrap them around the broken bone so that they do not move; then tie the bandage tightly to the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check each hour the binding, and if it loosens, then tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or itching in the area, or pain or an abscess, then hurry, and untie it, and apply a new dressing as needed by the circumstances; then reapply the poultice and tie it tightly until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the break in the ribs comes from their thick part behind, and at the front they are thin; and people feel this well during examination with both hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you place the fracture evenly, as is appropriate.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs inclines inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue; and it becomes sharp points, and quickly vomits a lot of blood, and this is serious illness, and the elderly often suffer greatly from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push out the rupture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this so that abscesses do not occur there if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have occurred, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place cupping glasses on the area to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the cups will draw the excesses to the area due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the layer around it, then treat it as one would for pleurisy, with food and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to cut into the place of the broken rib, and put an instrument underneath to protect the surface; then one must saw through the bone lightly, and then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, place cloths soaked in rose oil on them; and treat the area as needed for an abscess, and let the patient lie awake on their side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be well or not, pay attention if you see their hands soft, swollen, and dead-colored, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if they can move and feel well when pinched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient may be cured, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be well or not, pay attention if the feet are weakened, and if there are symptoms that are like those in the hands, and on the back there is bloating and involuntary evacuation; and when one turns them over onto their stomach, there is also involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wishes to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly; do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should apply it if there is a hot abscess, using rose oil or boiled egg oil until it subsides; then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, bind it with a cloth, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone should break, it must be treated on the chest; remove the bone, then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with an ointment that heals flesh until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the knuckle," place your left thumb inside it and align it as best you can with your other hand, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then compress it, and if there are any loose bones, cut them out and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there may be a slight shortening at the head; it fractures lengthwise, and inclines inward, causing pain to the patient in that place, and bruising, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, until you are above the break; and feel where the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, make it equal so that it has a natural appearance.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, where it inclines inward, make the patient lie on their belly until the restoration of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place the plaster on top, then put a stick of wood or cork over it, and hold the binder so that it does not move; and fill the area under the ribs until the flesh is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come up, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are appeased, and place what we said before on it; then return to the restoration process, and bind as is appropriate, if there is no adverse incident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a staff filled with healing ointment, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads with two ropes and pull them up, then seat the patient on a chair; then lay the broken arm on the staff, until it reaches the armpit, and place a curved piece of wood in between, then raise it with some heavy object or have an assistant hold it down; then place the fracture level with both hands, so that it returns as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lift the patient onto his uninjured side, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants that one should pull above the fracture at the hands, and the other below along the entire length of the arm, stretching each part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish for the extraction to be stronger, then remove the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the muscles on its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must place one ligament below the socket, and the other towards the side, below the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the side, then place one ligament lightly, without labor, until the fracture is level above the area, and above the side; then equalize the fracture as it should be, and compress it, unless abscesses cause issues.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses appear, do not compress it until the seventh day, and apply linen moistened in lard and rose oil until the abscesses subside; then compress it, and the manner of compressing is that you place a plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm up to the shoulder joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and wrap it with a cloth, and compress around the shoulder joint and the arm, so that the arm is in position, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place over the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one finger's width, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers' width on each side; then press upon the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, more firmly and less in spreading.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the arrangement of the splints and the binding as we have said, when you restore the broken member, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it tied up until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandage every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur at the site, where the new tissue cannot form because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is reduced, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.
