And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have described, then bind the patient's two feet together with a strong bandage under both heels and above both knees; then place the affected leg extended two palms longer than the other; then suspend him by his head from a post, and raise him off the ground two arm lengths; then instruct one helper to embrace the upper part of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging alongside the patient who firmly embraces the thigh, because now the joint will quickly return.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down, as we have said about him who has gilbositeit, and tightly bind one bandage on the diseased leg and another on the foot; then put two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then place a torch between the thighs of the patient in its form; and let pieces of moist cloths be placed around so that it does not burn the patient, then each minister should extend towards him, and the physician places his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the case of gilbositeit, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, as I have said; and place the healer's hand on the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and extend downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is to the side, it is not necessary to extend the affected leg downwards, nor raise it up in the air, but rather it should be as if the thigh were dislocated to the side, as we have described for lying on both thighs; and he should lie on his face, and the limb extended as we said before, and one must press on the joint towards the table; and it is right when the patient extends their legs, and they are even; then join the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind them firmly with a bandage so that the thigh does not move; and rest for three days or four, then unbind him, and put the plaster back on; and if you see that they are even, bind them as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk gently until the limb is restored.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not bend properly, you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is as follows: make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, then place your back against his chest, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, pull between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee forcefully; another assistant should straighten his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it bends properly at the thigh slightly; then apply a plaster, bind the leg firmly to the thigh for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient must not labor to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly positioned, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is set correctly
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tenderness in the area where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit straight, and hold the limb firmly by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then twice with the left hand, then extend it upwards, and forcefully push the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start over because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a board firmly in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around them so they do not move the patient; then hold the limb with your hands or a sling tied under the foot's neck; then both assistants extend equally, and the board should be steady between the patient’s thighs to prevent movement when extending; then place the dislocation in your hands evenly, and another assistant holds the healthy leg from behind, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, put the plaster and wads on, and bandage tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the heel, so that the bandages are not too tight; then leave him for two days or three, and if the bandaging loosens, tighten it again; then untie after the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful boils occur, you must relieve them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is at any joint of the back of the foot, you must have the patient sit on a flat place or on a table completely straight, and put your foot under what appears to be the joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when they are even, and nothing appears amiss, place a board two fists under the sole of the foot, then hold firmly, and leave for three days, then release; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not long experience, and if you are not compassionate and cautious, not bold; and use at first soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of health; and when there is hope, now reset the limb to its place, so that the hot abscess does not follow; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and treat the wound as it should be done with drying ointments; and if along with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones displaced, remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering into ways of fear according to what I have said, for this will bring you harm according to your Creator, and for the sake of wisdom of your art and of your body.
Amen	So be it
